### SPLIT_DESIGN_RATIONALE (1)

#### obs #168 — M10 pre-Phase-1 split design (M10 / M10b / M10c)

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** pre_phase_1_split_design
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-split-design-v1-20260522.md`

**description:**

> # M10 — Split design (3-way), v1
> 
> **Date:** 2026-05-22
> **Cluster as defined (v6 / 2026-05-05):** M10 — Guilt, Sin and Transgression (88 OWNER terms, 26 contributing registries, ~2,287 verses)
> **Decision:** Split into three sibling clusters before any Phase 1 work, on ontological grounds.
> 
> ---
> 
> ## 1. Why split
> 
> The 26 contributing registries assigned to M10 by v6 meaning-similarity cover three distinct ontological tracks of moral failure:
> 
> | Track | Question it answers | Lexical centre |
> |---|---|---|
> | **Act / state of failure** | *What did I do? What is my standing before God?* | sin, guilt, transgression, iniquity, rebellion |
> | **Character of evil** | *What kind of person are they? What is the moral nature of this conduct?* | evil, wickedness, abomination |
> | **Ritual / moral defilement** | *What state has this rendered me / this thing?* | impurity, defilement, uncleanness |
> 
> Per v2_8 §6.3.2 (verse-level relationship test) and §8.0 (sub-groups represent characteristics), forcing all three tracks through a single cluster would either:
> - collapse the three tracks into one sub-group structure and lose ontological precision, or
> - produce 3 top-level characteristics inside one cluster, which is the structural signature of an under-split cluster.
> 
> Splitting now, before Phase 1, is cheaper than splitting later. The cluster has `status='Not started'`, so no analytical work is invalidated.
> 
> ## 2. Split assignment (registry-level cuts)
> 
> ### M10 — Sin, Guilt and Transgression  (63 terms · 19 registries · ~1,475 V)
> 
> The act/state track: doing wrong, being guilty, breaking covenant, falling short.
> 
> | # | Reg | Word | Terms | V |
> |---|---:|---|---:|---:|
> | 1 |  73 | guilt ★ anchor | 16 | 965 |
> | 2 | 128 | rebellion | 5 | 138 |
> | 3 |  59 | faith (unfaithfulness terms ba.gad/ma.al) | 3 | 103 |
> | 4 |  89 | iniquity | 6 | 66 |
> | 5 | 147 | sin | 4 | 47 |
> | 6 |  31 | corruption (corrupt-acts) | 6 | 34 |
> | 7 | 162 | transgression | 4 | 30 |
> | 8 | 149 | slander (blasphemy-as-act) | 2 | 22 |
> | 9 | 120 | perverseness | 4 | 19 |
> | 10 |  98 | justice (injustice-acts) | 3 | 15 |
> | 11 |   2 | agony (cha.val/che.vel writhing-in-guilt) | 2 | 12 |
> | 12 |  51 | distress (a.ven trouble/iniquity) | 1 | 11 |
> | 13 | 111 | mercy (kip.pu.rim atonement, paired with sin) | 1 | 8 |
> | 14 |  40 | deceit (deleazō entice) | 1 | 3 |
> | 15 |   6 | anointing (te.vel perversion) | 1 | 2 |
> | 16 |  71 | grief (pu.qah) | 1 | 1 |
> | 17 |  81 | hypocrisy (sunupokrinomai) | 1 | 1 |
> | 18 | 134 | renewal (cha.loph decay/destruction) | 1 | 1 |
> | 19 | 190 | contempt (nav.lut lewdness) | 1 | 1 |
> 
> ### M10b — Wickedness, Evil and Abomination  (17 terms · 4 registries · ~537 V)
> 
> The character track: what kind of person, what kind of conduct in its nature.
> 
> | # | Reg | Word | Terms | V |
> |---|---:|---|---:|---:|
> | 1 | 172 | wickedness ★ anchor (ra.sha, mir.sha.at) | 2 | 181 |
> | 2 |   1 | abomination (to.e.vah, shiq.quts, bdelugma, bdeluktos) | 4 | 145 |
> | 3 |  57 | evil ★ anchor (ponēros, kakia, adikia, ponēria, blasfēmeō, kakopoios, atopos, faulos, re.sha) | 9 | 126 |
> | 4 | 151 | sorrow (a.ven, ro.a as evil-character/condition) | 2 | 85 |
> 
> ### M10c — Defilement and Impurity  (8 terms · 3 registries · ~275 V)
> 
> The defilement track: ritual + moral uncleanness, separation language.
> 
> | # | Reg | Word | Terms | V |
> |---|---:|---|---:|---:|
> | 1 |  86 | impurity ★ anchor (ta.me, nid.dah, akatharsia, akathartos) | 5 | 270 |
> | 2 |  41 | defilement (molunō, molusmos) | 2 | 4 |
> | 3 | 115 | passion (miasmos) | 1 | 1 |
> 
> ## 3. Cluster-row metadata for new siblings
> 
> | Field | M10 (revised) | M10b (new) | M10c (new) |
> |---|---|---|---|
> | `cluster_code` | M10 | M10b | M10c |
> | `description` | Sin, Guilt and Transgression | Wickedness, Evil and Abomination | Defilement and Impurity |
> | `short_name` | Sin | Wickedness | Defilement |
> | `source` | meaning_v2 | meaning_v2_split_20260522 | meaning_v2_split_20260522 |
> | `bucket` | NAMED | NAMED | NAMED |
> | `status` | Not started | Not started | Not started |
> | `version` | v6 | v6 | v6 |
> | `gloss` | (regenerate from members) | (regenerate from members) | (regenerate from members) |
> 
> ## 4. Term migration counts
> 
> ```
> Before:  M10 = 88 OWNER terms / 26 registries / ~2,287 V
> After:   M10  = 63 terms / 19 registries / ~1,475 V
>          M10b = 17 terms /  4 registries /   ~537 V
>          M10c =  8 terms /  3 registries /   ~275 V
> Total preserved: 63 + 17 + 8 = 88 ✓
> ```
> 
> ## 5. Borderline terms — recorded for new-cluster Phase 1
> 
> These calls were made at registry-level to keep the apply script simple. The receiving cluster's Phase 1 may reroute individual terms:
> 
> - **R057.G0987 blasfēmeō** (verb, "to blaspheme") was moved with R057 → M10b, but R149 blasfēmia/blasfēmos stayed in M10. M10b Phase 1 should consider whether to push blasfēmeō back to M10 to keep the blasphemy lemma family together.
> - **R057.G0093 adikia** ("unrighteousness/wickedness") and **R098.G0094 adikos** ("unjust") split across M10b and M10 by registry. Same root family — Phase 1 in each cluster should record the cross-reference.
> - **R051.H0205H a.ven** stayed in M10 (distress home) but **R151.H0205G a.ven** moved with R151 → M10b. Same lexeme, different home-registry assignments in v6. Cross-cluster handoff observation required.
> - **R134.H2475 cha.loph** ("change/decay") in M10 vs **R031.H4893B-H4889 mash.chet/mash.chit** ("destroyer") in M10 — coherent stay-call; just noting destruction-semantics is split between M10 (acts) and other M-clusters (not split here).
> 
> ## 6. Apply order
> 
> 1. INSERT cluster rows M10b, M10c.
> 2. UPDATE `cluster` SET description='Sin, Guilt and Transgression', short_name='Sin' WHERE cluster_code='M10'.
> 3. UPDATE `mti_terms.cluster_code` to 'M10b' for 17 terms (registries 1, 57, 151, 172).
> 4. UPDATE `mti_terms.cluster_code` to 'M10c' for 8 terms (registries 41, 86, 115).
> 5. Regenerate gloss strings for all three from current member terms.
> 6. Verify totals: M10=63, M10b=17, M10c=8.
> 
> Script: `scripts/_apply_m10_split_3way_20260522.py`
> 
> ## 7. Downstream
> 
> - Cluster overview report: refresh once split is applied — should show 16 clusters now (M10 stayed, M10b/M10c added).
> - Phase 1 work on each cluster is independent and can begin in any order.
> - M10c is small (8 terms / 275 V) but has a clear anchor (impurity, 270 V) and survives §8.6 distribution gate easily.
> 
> ---
> 
> *Split design v1 — apply pending researcher confirmation already given (Option A 3-way split, 2026-05-22).*

### SUBGROUP_DESIGN_RATIONALE (10)

#### obs #158 — M10 sub-group design (original) — §1. Characteristics identified

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> Nine distinct inner-being faculties/states are evidenced by the M10 meaning corpus. These are derived from reading the Pass A meanings across all major-corpus terms.
> 
> ### Characteristic 1 — Sin as committed act
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The will in the moment of moral failure — sinning as a directed act against God, another person, or oneself. This is the *active* dimension: the person doing wrong, the conscience registering a committed fault, the will that defected, disobeyed, or violated. The meanings in this register describe sinning as something one does (verb-form vocabulary dominant), with the inner dimension being the volitional moral failure — conscience struck, the will that chose wrongly, the act that now requires accounting for.
> 
> Key evidence: cha.ta meanings covering confession (Pharaoh — Exo 9:27; David — 2Sa 12:13), protective restraint (Exo 20:20 — God's terrifying presence to deter sinning), interpersonal wrong (Mat 18:15 — sinning against a brother), and volitional defection (Deu 9:16 — quickly turning from the commanded way). Also: hamartanō's 37-verse corpus covering the full range of sinning-as-act; the slander/blasphemy terms (speech-act register of sinning); enticement vocabulary (deleazō — the mechanism that leads the inner person to sin through desire); the hypocrisy term (sinful act of false-appearance).
> 
> ### Characteristic 2 — Sin as moral condition / state
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* Sin as an objective reality that the inner person carries — not primarily the moment of doing, but the condition of being under sin, burdened by it, dominated by it, needing it removed. The meanings in this register describe sin as a thing that accumulates (Exo 32:30 — great sin requiring atonement), is recorded against the person (Rev 18:5 — crimes heaped to heaven), enslaves (Joh 8:34 — practicing sin makes one its slave), and constitutes a death-state (Eph 2:1 — dead in trespasses). The inner-being characteristic is the condition of the person *under* sin, not the act of sinning.
> 
> Key evidence: hamartia's extensive corpus (universal human condition, bondage, power — Rom 3:9; Joh 8:34), chat.tat H2403B (sin as predatory force crouching at the door — Gen 4:7; sin as persistent king-pattern — 1Ki 16:31), paraptōma (death-state from trespass — Eph 2:1/5; Col 2:13), rish.ah (wickedness as defining inner condition — Isa 9:18; Mal 1:4), and the atonement/sin-offering terms (kip.pu.rim, chat.tat H2403H) whose verses reflect sin-as-condition requiring covering.
> 
> ### Characteristic 3 — The sinner as moral character
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The constitutive inner identity of the person defined by sin — not the act (Char 1) or the condition (Char 2), but the person whose character is marked by sin as their essential moral description. The meanings in this register describe sinners as a recognisable social-moral category (Mat 9:10/11), as those whose inner character is sinfulness (Luk 5:8 — "I am a sinful man"; Rom 5:8 — "while we were still sinners"), as those constituted sinners (Rom 5:19 — imputed inner status), and as persons whose persistent pattern of sinning discloses their allegiance (1Jo 3:6/8/9). The characteristic is the *identity* dimension: what kind of person this is at their moral core.
> 
> Key evidence: hamartōlos (45V — the sinner as social-moral category, as object of Jesus's ministry, as constituted inner state), chat.ta (19V — habitual sinner as extreme moral character, including Sodom's men, Jeroboam's generational pattern).
> 
> ### Characteristic 4 — Guilt as inner-being state
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The conscience's recognition of moral liability before God — the subjective inner experience of being guilty, of bearing a wrong that cannot be hidden, that weighs on the spirit, that demands response. The meanings in this register describe guilt as recognised (Gen 42:21 — brothers recognise their past cruelty as guilt in present distress; Gen 44:16 — guilt exposed by God; Lev 5:5 — realising guilt obligates confession), as a weight carried (Ezr 9:6 — guilt risen above the head; Psa 38:4/18 — iniquity as heavy burden on the will; Psa 51:5 — born into guilt; 1Sa 25:31 — conscience stumbling from guilt), as indelible before God (Jer 2:22 — no soap can remove it). The characteristic is the internal moral experience of guilt.
> 
> Key evidence: a.sham (31V — guilt-recognition process in conscience), a.shem (3V — guilty state), ash.mah (17V — guiltiness as inner burden/weight), a.von H5771H guilt sub-entry (27V — guilt as hidden, transferable, indelible burden), a.von H5771I punishment sub-entry (18V — guilt's punitive weight borne), pu.qah (1V — staggering of conscience from potential bloodguilt).
> 
> ### Characteristic 5 — Iniquity as accumulated moral crime
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* Iniquity as the inner dimension of accumulated moral wrongdoing — crime in its moral-spiritual sense, not merely legal. The meanings evidence iniquity as a measured accumulation not yet full (Gen 15:16), as a generational inheritance (Exo 20:5 — visited on descendants), as a heart-seated reality (Eze 14:3/4/7 — idols taken into the heart), as a self-rotting force (Lev 26:39 — wasting away in iniquity in exile), as a burden requiring confession before restoration is possible (Lev 26:40/41). This is distinct from guilt (Char 4) in that guilt is the subjective recognition/experience, while iniquity-as-crime is the objective moral accumulation — the inner store of wrongdoing before God.
> 
> Key evidence: a.von H5771G crime sub-entry (162V — the full iniquity-as-crime corpus), al.vah H5932 (1V — iniquity at Gibeah as moral character of a community).
> 
> ### Characteristic 6 — Transgression / rebellion as deliberate boundary-crossing
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The willful defiance of known moral or covenantal order — the inner act of the will that rebels, crosses a boundary it knows to exist, or deliberately breaches a covenant it is party to. The meanings consistently evidence this as *knowing* transgression: the nations' accumulated offenses (Amo 1–2 — transgressions that cross a threshold of divine tolerance), the people's deliberate departure (Isa 1:2 — children rebelling against a nurturing father), the will that multiplies transgressions (Isa 59:12/13 — rebellion as initiating act), Adam's paradigmatic violation of a direct command (Rom 5:14). The characteristic is the volitional dimension of conscious rebellion.
> 
> Key evidence: pe.sha H6588 (90V — the primary OT transgression corpus), pa.sha H6586 (37V — to transgress as rebellion-act), parabasis/parabatēs/parabainō (16V — NT law-crossing vocabulary), paraptōma (14V — trespass in its Pauline meaning, particularly the Adam-paradigm passages), sa.rah H5627 (8V — revolt/rebellion against God), apostasia G0646 (1V — apostasy as covenantal defection).
> 
> ### Characteristic 7 — Faithlessness / treachery as wilful covenant-breaking sin
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The inner disposition of deliberate unfaithfulness — the will that breaks covenantal loyalty, betrays a trust, or acts treacherously against God or persons. This is distinct from generic sin-as-act (Char 1) and from transgression/rebellion (Char 6) in that it specifically names the *relational* dimension of sinful moral failure: the betrayal of a bond that was known and was owed. The meanings evidence treachery as a settled inner character (Isa 48:8 — constitutional unfaithfulness known to God before birth; Isa 24:16 — threefold emphasis on treachery as intensified inner character); as covenant-breaking toward God (Hos 6:7 — at Adam; Mal 2:15/16 — guard the spirit against faithlessness toward a wife); and as a community-wide moral disposition (Jer 9:2 — treachery so pervasive the prophet wishes to flee; 2Ch 36:14 — corporate unfaithfulness defiling the temple).
> 
> Key evidence: ba.gad H0898 (39V — to act treacherously; cross-register M13/M31), ma.al H4603 (34V — to be unfaithful; cross-register M13/M31), ma.al H4604 (28V — unfaithfulness; cross-register M13/M31).
> 
> ### Characteristic 8 — Perversion / moral corruption as inner-being inversion
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The inner state or disposition of moral distortion — twisting what is right, corrupting what was good, inverting the moral order. The meanings evidence this as operating through speech (Pro 2:12/14 — twisted words; Pro 10:31/32 — perversity in the tongue; 1Cor 15:33 — corrupting good morals through bad company), through the mind's faculty (Pro 12:8 — twisted mind inviting contempt; 2Cor 11:3 — corrupting the mind's devotion to Christ; 1Ti 6:5 — mind depraved by corruption), through deliberate inner scheming (Pro 6:14 — perversity originates in the heart and drives continual evil-devising; Eph 4:22 — the old self corrupted through deceitful desires), and as a comprehensive inner moral degeneracy (Jer 2:21 — the vine turned wild from within; Eph 4:22; Jude 10 — destroyed from within by what is acted on instinctively). The characteristic is the *inversion* dimension: moral character that has been twisted away from what is right.
> 
> Key evidence: tah.pu.khah H8419 (10V — perversity as deep inner moral inversion), a.vah H5753B (10V — to pervert as deliberate moral distortion), a.vah H5753A (6V — to twist with M03 cross-register on anguish register), sa.laph H5557 (6V — perverting justice through bribery), ftheirō G5351 (7V — moral corruption active in the inner life), fthora G5356 (8V — corruption as inner bondage; bodily-decay cross-register M23/M35), diaftheirō G1311 (3V — depraved mind), sur H5494 (2V — degenerating from God), te.vel H8397 (2V — sexual perversion), la.zut H3891 (1V — perversity in speech), ho.phekh H2017 (1V — cognitive inversion), mut.teh H4297 (1V — structural injustice as moral distortion), cha.val H2254B (5V — moral corruption against God; M03 cross-register), nav.lut H5040 (1V — lewdness as shameful moral disposition; M07 cross-register).
> 
> ### Characteristic 9 — Injustice as moral failure of right conduct
> 
> *What specific inner-being faculty or state does this evidence?* The inner state/disposition of doing what is wrong toward persons — unjust conduct, unjust character, the person whose moral faculty is bent toward wrongdoing against others. The meanings evidence injustice as arising from inner moral disposition (Psa 53:1 — fool's heart-denial of God produces unjust conduct; Psa 58:2 — devised in the heart before enacted by hands), as a fixed character trait (Luk 16:10 — unjust person is unjust across all scales, showing it as a stable inner disposition), as the opposite of righteousness (Deu 32:4 — God's character is without injustice; 1Pe 3:18 — the unjust for whom Christ died). M26 cross-register throughout: injustice is the structural opposite of righteousness, placing it in ongoing dialogue with M26. The M10 characteristic is the sinful inner moral-failure of justice-denial.
> 
> Key evidence: a.vel H5766A (20V — injustice in judicial, relational, characterological contexts), av.lah H5766B (32V — injustice as wilful wrongdoing arising from inner corruption), adikos G0094 (11V — unjust as stable inner moral disposition), av.val H5767 (5V — unjust one as moral character), a.vil H5760 (1V — ungodly lawless person), adikēma G0092 (3V — crime as moral-legal violation).
> 
> ---

#### obs #159 — M10 sub-group design (original) — §2. Sub-group design

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> Nine sub-groups (one per characteristic) + one BOUNDARY sub-group. No volume-split required: the largest characteristic (sin-as-condition, est. ~295V) is well below the 530V gate.
> 
> Sub-group codes: M10-A through M10-I (characteristics 1–9), M10-BND (boundary).
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-A — Sin as committed act
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-A  
> **label:** Sin as committed act  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 1 — Sin as committed act  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the act-of-sinning characteristic: the will in the moment of moral failure, sinning as a relational act directed against God, another person, or oneself. The inner-being content is volitional — the conscience recognising a committed fault, the will that defected or chose wrongly, the act now requiring acknowledgment and accounting for. The corpus covers sinning as confession (the person who names what they have done), as deterrence (the inner person who must be restrained from sinning), as interpersonal wrong (sinning against a brother, a master, the Lord), and as habitual pattern of the will. Specialised verbal registers include: slander/blasphemy as sin-of-speech originating in the heart (G0988, G0989), enticement as the mechanism leading inner desire into sin (G1185), and hypocrisy as the sinful act of false-appearance (G4942). The characteristic is the active dimension — the moment and act of moral failure.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** cha.ta H2398 (201V), hamartanō G0264 (37V), pa.sha H6586 (partial — rebellion-against-God verses; see §3 multi-faceted terms), blasfēmia G0988 (18V), pa.sha H6586 (37V, fully), blasfēmos G0989 (4V), deleazō G1185 (3V), sunupokrinomai G4942 (1V), nav.lut H5040 (1V), apostasia G0646 (absorbed — defection-as-act register; see §3)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~265–275V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-B — Sin as moral condition
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-B  
> **label:** Sin as moral condition / state  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 2 — Sin as moral condition / state  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the condition-of-sin characteristic: sin as an objective moral reality that the inner person carries — not primarily the act of doing wrong, but the state of being under sin's dominion, burdened by it, enslaved by it, needing it removed or covered. The inner-being content is the person's moral ontology — what they are under sin rather than what they did. The corpus covers sin as accumulated moral weight recorded against the person, as enslaving force mastering the will (Joh 8:34), as universal human condition into which all are born (Rom 5:12/19), as death-state from which God must raise (Eph 2:1/5), and as reality that must be atoned for or covered before the person can stand before God. The atonement/sin-offering terms (kip.pu.rim, chat.tat H2403H) are placed here because their meanings evidence sin-as-condition requiring covering — the problem that atonement addresses. Wickedness-as-inner-condition (rish.ah) also belongs here as the state-dimension of sinful moral character.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** hamartia G0266 (105V), chat.tat H2403B (159V), paraptōma G3900 (14V), chat.ta.ah H2401 (8V), chat.ta.ah H2403A (2V), hamartēma G0265 (4V), kip.pu.rim H3725 (8V; M11 cross-register flag travels with), chat.tat H2403H sin-offering (4V; M11 cross-register flag travels with), rish.ah H7564 (4V), al.vah H5932 (1V — iniquity-as-condition register, 1v only)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~309V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-C — The sinner as moral character
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-C  
> **label:** The sinner as moral character  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 3 — The sinner as moral character  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the identity-of-sin characteristic: the constitutive inner moral identity of the person described as a sinner — not what they did (Char 1) or the condition they are in (Char 2), but what kind of person they are at their moral core. The inner-being content is characterological — the sinner as recognisable moral category, as the person whose habitual pattern of sinning discloses their deepest allegiance (1Jo 3:6/8/9), as someone whose very being was formed in sinfulness (Rom 5:19 — constituted sinners by one man's disobedience), as the object of Jesus's explicit ministry precisely because their character is what it is (Mar 2:17). The corpus covers the sinner as social-moral category (Mat 9:10/11), as person owning their sinful identity (Luk 5:8), as those constituted sinners (Rom 5:8/19), and as habitual extreme sinners whose moral character is total (Gen 13:13 — Sodom; 1Sa 15:18 — the Amalekites; Amo 9:8 — the sinful kingdom).
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** hamartōlos G0268 (45V), chat.ta H2400 (19V)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** 64V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-D — Guilt as inner-being state
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-D  
> **label:** Guilt as inner-being state  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 4 — Guilt as inner-being state  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the guilt-experience characteristic: the conscience's recognition of moral liability before God — the subjective inner experience of being guilty, of having wronged God or another, of carrying a weight that cannot be hidden from God's sight. The inner-being content is the conscience in its guilt-awareness mode: the moment of realisation (Lev 5:2/3/4/5 — guilt arising when a hidden violation becomes known), the weight of acknowledged guilt (Psa 38:4/18; Ezr 9:6 — guilt risen above the head), the indelibility of guilt before God (Jer 2:22 — no soap removes it), and the grace of guilt's removal (Isa 6:7 — guilt taken away by divine act). The a.von punishment sub-entry belongs here rather than in Char 5 because its meanings primarily evidence the punitive burden of guilt as inner experience (Gen 4:13 — Cain's unbearable weight; Eze 4:4–6 — physically borne). The staggering-of-conscience term (pu.qah) belongs here as a single-verse expression of guilt-awareness.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** a.sham H0816 (31V), a.shem H0818 (3V), ash.mah H0819 (17V), a.von H5771H guilt sub-entry (27V), a.von H5771I punishment sub-entry (18V), pu.qah H6330 (1V; M03 cross-register flag travels with)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** 97V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-E — Iniquity as accumulated moral crime
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-E  
> **label:** Iniquity as accumulated moral crime  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 5 — Iniquity as accumulated moral crime  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the iniquity-as-crime characteristic: the inner dimension of accumulated moral wrongdoing — crime in its moral-spiritual sense, the store of inner wrongdoing that exists before God as a measured, generational, heart-seated reality. Distinct from guilt (Char 4, which is the subjective recognition/experience) in that this characteristic addresses iniquity as the objective moral accumulation — what is known by God even when hidden from others (Psa 90:8 — iniquities and secret sins set in God's light), what has built up over generations (Exo 20:5), what is seated in the heart (Eze 14:3/4/7 — idols taken into the heart as the seat of iniquity), and what must be confessed before restoration is possible (Lev 26:40/41 — humble heart as prerequisite for making amends). The inner-being dimension is the person's moral account before God: the crime-weight they carry whether they feel it or not.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** a.von H5771G crime sub-entry (162V)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** 162V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-F — Transgression / rebellion as deliberate boundary-crossing
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-F  
> **label:** Transgression / rebellion as deliberate boundary-crossing  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 6 — Transgression / rebellion as deliberate boundary-crossing  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the transgression-as-rebellion characteristic: the willful defiance of known moral or covenantal order — the inner act of the will that rebels, crosses a boundary it knows to exist, or deliberately breaches a covenant or law it is party to. The inner-being content is volitional transgression: the will that knowingly steps over a line (parabasis — law-violation requiring a law to violate — Rom 4:15), the heart from which transgression speaks (Psa 36:1), the accumulated rebellions of nations that cross a threshold of divine tolerance (Amo 1:3–2:6), Adam's paradigmatic conscious violation (Rom 5:14). The salient inner-being characteristic is the *knowing* dimension — this is not inadvertent sin but wilful boundary-crossing. The revolt (sa.rah) and apostasy terms belong here, sharing the rebellion-against-known-authority register.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** pe.sha H6588 (90V), parabasis G3847 (7V), parabatēs G3848 (5V), parabainō G3845 (4V), paraptōma G3900 — rebellion-register verses (partial — most paraptōma goes to Char 2; see §3 multi-faceted terms), sa.rah H5627 (8V), apostasia G0646 (1V — if not fully in Char 1)
> 
> **Note on pa.sha:** The 37 verses of the to-transgress verb split between Char 1 (the rebellion-as-sinful-act register) and Char 6 (the deliberate-political-breach register). The majority of pa.sha verses evidence the rebellion-against-God sense rather than generic sin-as-act, so primary assignment is Char 6 with Char 1 as secondary. See §3.
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~120–130V (after pa.sha primary allocation here, paraptōma partial split)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-G — Faithlessness / treachery as wilful covenant-breaking
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-G  
> **label:** Faithlessness / treachery as covenant-breaking sin  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 7 — Faithlessness / treachery as wilful covenant-breaking sin  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the faithlessness characteristic: the inner disposition of deliberate unfaithfulness — the will that breaks covenantal loyalty, betrays a trust, or acts treacherously against God or persons. The distinguishing feature of this characteristic within M10 is the *relational* dimension of sinful moral failure: betrayal of a bond that was known, owed, and willfully broken. The inner-being content is the disposition of the will toward infidelity — treachery as a settled inner character (Isa 48:8 — constitutional unfaithfulness; Isa 24:16 — threefold intensified treachery), unfaithfulness deepening under pressure rather than breaking (2Ch 28:22 — Ahaz more faithless in distress), and the call to guard the spirit against faithlessness (Mal 2:15 — vigilance in the spirit against treachery toward a wife). The M13/M31 cross-register flags (faithfulness, faith) travel with all three terms; their M10 representation is the betrayal-as-sin dimension.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** ba.gad H0898 (39V; M13/M31 cross-register), ma.al H4603 (34V; M13/M31 cross-register), ma.al H4604 (28V; M13/M31 cross-register)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** 101V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-H — Perversion / moral corruption as inner inversion
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-H  
> **label:** Perversion / moral corruption as inner inversion  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 8 — Perversion / moral corruption as inner-being inversion  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the perversion/corruption characteristic: the inner state or disposition of moral distortion — twisting what is right, corrupting what was good, inverting the moral order from within. The inner-being content operates at the level of the person's inner moral faculty: perversity originating in the heart and driving continual evil-devising (Pro 6:14), the mind that becomes depraved (1Ti 6:5 — corruption penetrating the seat of understanding), the old self corrupted through deceitful desires (Eph 4:22), the person destroyed from within by what they act on instinctively (Jude 10). The characteristic is the *inversion* dimension: the inner moral character that has been twisted away from what is right, producing distorted speech, distorted judgment (Exo 23:8 — bribery corrupting judicial discernment), and distorted conduct. Also carries: the sexual-perversion terms (te.vel — violation of created/family order), the moral-degeneracy terms (sur — the vine turning wild from within), and the lewdness term (nav.lut — shameful inner disposition; M07 cross-register).
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** tah.pu.khah H8419 (10V), a.vah H5753B (10V), a.vah H5753A (6V; M03 cross-register), sa.laph H5557 (6V), ftheirō G5351 (7V), fthora G5356 (8V; M23/M35 cross-register), diaftheirō G1311 (3V), sur H5494 (2V), te.vel H8397 (2V), la.zut H3891 (1V), ho.phekh H2017 (1V), mut.teh H4297 (1V), cha.val H2254B (5V; M03 cross-register), nav.lut H5040 (1V; M07 cross-register)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** 63V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-I — Injustice as moral failure of right conduct
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-I  
> **label:** Injustice as moral failure of right conduct  
> **Characteristic:** Characteristic 9 — Injustice as moral failure of right conduct  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the injustice characteristic: the inner state/disposition of doing what is wrong toward persons — unjust conduct, unjust character, the moral faculty bent toward wrongdoing against others and against right order. The inner-being content is the disposition toward injustice: injustice devised in the heart before enacted by hands (Psa 58:2), injustice as a fixed character trait expressed across all scales of conduct (Luk 16:10), injustice as the inner condition from which the person cannot escape God's moral accounting (Act 24:15; 2Pe 2:9), and injustice as the opposite of righteousness (Deu 32:4 — God's character is without injustice; Rom 3:5 — God tested against the standard of justice). The M26 cross-register (Righteousness and Justice) flags travel with all terms in this sub-group; their M10 representation is the sinful-conduct-against-right-order dimension.
> 
> **Terms assigned as primary:** a.vel H5766A (20V; M26 cross-register), av.lah H5766B (32V; M26 cross-register), adikos G0094 (11V; M26 cross-register), av.val H5767 (5V; M26 cross-register), a.vil H5760 (1V), adikēma G0092 (3V)
> 
> **Estimated verse volume:** 72V
> 
> ---
> 
> ### M10-BND — Boundary
> 
> **subgroup_code:** M10-BND  
> **label:** Boundary — analytically undecided terms  
> **core_description:** This sub-group carries the 6 BOUNDARY-verdict terms from Phase 3. Five verses are routed here (4 from H0205H a.ven + 1 from H2256D che.vel); the remaining 4 BOUNDARY terms (H4889 mash.chit, H4892 mash.chet, H4893B ma.she.chat, H2475 cha.loph) have zero relevant verses and attach as member-terms without verse contributions. Phase 8.5 will resolve each BOUNDARY term to SET-ASIDE, ROUTE-TO-CLUSTER, or PROMOTE-TO-SUBGROUP. The analytical questions per term are recorded in the Phase 3 verdict document. Note: Pro 12:21 (a.ven borderline verse) is NOT in the corpus — no vc row exists; it is not routed here. Mic 2:10 (cha.val) has been resolved to relevant and routes to M10-H (see §7 of Phase 3 verdict).
> 
> **Terms carrying BOUNDARY verdict:** H0205H a.ven (4V), H2256D che.vel (1V), H4889 mash.chit (0V), H4892 mash.chet (0V), H4893B ma.she.chat (0V), H2475 cha.loph (0V)
> 
> **BOUNDARY verse volume:** 5V (trivially 0.38% of substantive corpus — within §8.4.1 gate)
> 
> ---

#### obs #160 — M10 sub-group design (original) — §3. Multi-faceted terms

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> Terms whose verses span more than one sub-group (primary + secondary assignment):
> 
> ### pa.sha H6586 — to transgress (37V)
> - **Primary:** M10-F (transgression/rebellion) — the majority of verses evidence deliberate rebellion against God or covenantal authority (Isa 1:2; Jer 2:8/29; Eze 2:3; Psa 37:38/51:13; Isa 43:27/48:8)
> - **Secondary:** M10-A (sin-as-act) — approximately 10 verses use the term for political revolt sense (2Ki 1:1; 8:20/22; 2Ch 21:8/10; 2Ch 10:19; 1Ki 12:19; 2Ki 3:5/7) where the inner-being register is the wilful-defection-as-sinful-act rather than the rebellion-against-God register
> - **Split rule:** primary M10-F; secondary M10-A for the Moab/Edom/political-revolt verses
> 
> ### paraptōma G3900 — trespass (14V)
> - **Primary:** M10-B (sin-as-condition) — the majority of verses evidence trespass in its condition/state register (Eph 2:1/5; Col 2:13 — dead in trespasses; 2Cor 5:19 — trespasses creating alienation; Gal 6:1 — caught in a trespass)
> - **Secondary:** M10-F (transgression/rebellion) — the Adam-paradigm verses (Rom 5:15/16/17/18/20) evidence trespass as the foundational wilful boundary-crossing that set the pattern
> - **Split rule:** Adam-paradigm verses (Rom 5:15–20) → M10-F primary; remaining (Rom 4:25; Rom 11:11/12; 2Cor 5:19; Gal 6:1; Eph 1:7; Eph 2:1/5; Col 2:13) → M10-B primary
> 
> ### apostasia G0646 — apostasy (1V)
> - **Primary:** M10-A (sin-as-act) — the single verse Act 21:21 (apostasy as accusation of teaching Jews to forsake covenant identity) evidences a sinful-act register more than a rebellion/boundary-crossing register
> - No secondary; single verse fully to M10-A
> 
> ### pu.qah H6330 — staggering (1V)
> - **Primary:** M10-D (guilt-as-inner-state) — conscience stumbling from guilt; M03 cross-register flag travels with
> - No secondary; single verse fully to M10-D
> 
> ---

#### obs #161 — M10 sub-group design (original) — §4. SPLIT_SUBGROUP flags

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> No SPLIT_SUBGROUP cases identified. No sub-group was found to contain VCG-level registers serving two distinct characteristics within the same lexical group. The closest candidate was pa.sha H6586 (which spans rebellion-against-God and political-revolt registers), but these are handled as a multi-faceted term assignment rather than a SPLIT_SUBGROUP, because the two registers belong to different sub-groups — the term itself does not evidence two characteristics within the same VCG structure.
> 
> ---

All sub-groups are well within the 530V gate.*

#### obs #163 — M10 sub-group design REVISION — §1. Candidate characteristics identified

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design_revision
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5 b/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-revision-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> Each characteristic is a single, named inner-being faculty or operation evidenced across multiple verses.
> 
> ### Char-R1 — Wilful sinning
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** The will committing a known wrong — sinning as a deliberate relational act directed against God, another person, or the self, where the person knows what they are doing and does it.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Deliberateness is present; the will is not ignorant or enticed but choosing.  
> **Keyword family:** `defection wilful` (16), `sin committed` (8), `sin relational` (8), `will defecting` (10), `defection willful` (15)  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~55V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primary  
> **Sample anchors:** Gen 39:9 (Joseph names it as sinning against God), Jos 7:20 (Achan's deliberate confession), 2Sa 12:13 (David: "I have sinned against the Lord"), Heb 10:26 (sinning deliberately after knowing truth), Dan 9:5 (cascade of confessed wilful failures)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R2 — Unintentional sinning
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin committed without deliberate intent — violation that is real and morally consequential even though the inner person did not consciously defy God's command; once it surfaces to awareness, conscience is engaged and remedy is required.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Ignorance or inadvertence at the time of the act; awareness comes after.  
> **Keyword family:** `violation inadvertent` (paired with `sin real` 4x, `ignorance` 3x), `unintentional violation`, `sin real`, `realization post-act`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~32V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primary (Lev 4–6 block)  
> **Sample anchors:** Lev 4:2 (unintentional; still real sin), Lev 5:17 (sinned unknowingly yet bears iniquity), Num 15:27 (unintentional sin still requires offering), Num 22:34 (Balaam: sin from ignorance requiring acknowledgment), 1Sa 14:33 (ritual transgression arising from urgency not defiance)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R3 — Confession: the conscience naming sin
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** The moment the inner person names a committed sin as sin — first-person confession, corporate declaration, or the conscience voicing an act already done. The faculty at work is conscience-in-confessional-mode: the will owns what was done.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Looking back at a completed act and naming it; distinct from guilt-recognition (which is the felt weight) and from repentance (which is the turning).  
> **Keyword family:** `guilt acknowledged` (25), `sin acknowledged` (11), `confession verbal` (8), `confession corporate` (8), `conscience naming` (10)  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~42V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primary  
> **Sample anchors:** Exo 9:27 (Pharaoh: "I have sinned"), Num 21:7 (people: "we have sinned"), 1Sa 7:6 (Israel's corporate confession), Dan 9:5–15 (Daniel's fourfold layered confession), Luk 15:18–21 (prodigal's planned and spoken confession)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R4 — Conscience suppression and self-deception
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** The inner person who does not recognize, denies, or suppresses awareness of their own sinful state — conscience absent, self-blinded, or actively claiming innocence where guilt is real. The faculty is conscience in its suppressed or inverted state.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Not ignorance (Char-R2) but suppression — the person has enough information to know but refuses to see; distinguished from wilful sinning (Char-R1) by the deception of the self about one's own state.  
> **Keyword family:** `conscience suppressed` (16), `self-deception` (10), `conscience absent` (10), `awareness lacking` (3 co-occ with `self-blindness`), `innocence claimed` (15 — especially when false)  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~28V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primarily, some M10-B  
> **Sample anchors:** Jer 2:35 (sinning compounded by inner denial of having sinned), Jer 16:10 (people fail to recognize their own sinning), 1Jo 1:10 (denying sinfulness = making God a liar), Ecc 8:12 (sinner repeatedly does evil, treats prosperity as vindication), Pro 30:20 (eats, wipes mouth: "I have done no wrong")
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R5 — Refusal to repent: departure withheld
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** The will that persistently refuses to turn from a sinful course — not ignorance, not occasional lapse, but the established inner orientation of choosing to remain in sin when departure is available and known to be required. The characteristic is the will's active withholding of turning.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Turning is known, available, and withheld — distinct from habitual defection (which is pattern-repetition) by the specific element of refusal when confronted.  
> **Keyword family:** `turning withheld` (9), `departure refused` (14 across both sub-groups), `will refusing` (12), `sin persisting` + `turning withheld` (3 co-occ), `will clinging` (3 co-occ with `departure refused`)  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~35V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primary; some M10-B  
> **Sample anchors:** 2Ki 3:3 (Jehoram clung to Jeroboam's sin), 2Ki 15:18 (Menahem did not depart all his days), Eze 18:24 (turning from righteousness back to sin — the reversal of departure), Heb 3:17 (sinned in wilderness, prolonged defiance), 1Jo 3:6 (continuing to sin reveals the person has never truly known Christ)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R6 — Habitual defection: sin as settled pattern
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin as a recurring, established pattern of the will — not a single act but a way of living; the will repeatedly chooses the same wrong course, making sinning a habitual orientation. The characteristic is the will's settled direction toward sin.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Pattern and repetition over time — distinguished from refusal-to-repent (Char-R5) by the temporal-accumulative dimension rather than the specific moment of refusal.  
> **Keyword family:** `defection habitual` (19), `sin habitual` (9), `defection habitual` + `sin persistent` (3 co-occ), `sin persisting` (3 co-occ with `turning withheld`), `defection repeated`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~30V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primary; some M10-B  
> **Sample anchors:** Hos 4:7 (sinning intensifies with prosperity — compulsive escalation), Hos 8:11 (sinning ritualized and self-reinforcing), Hos 13:2 (sinning more and more — compulsion deepening), 1Jo 3:8 (habitual practice discloses allegiance), 1Ti 5:20 (persisting in sin — will entrenched)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R7 — Contagious sin: leadership transmitting moral defection
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin as a moral direction set by a leader whose inner commitment to wrongdoing is transmitted to those under authority — the will of those who follow is bent by the influence of a corrupting leader. The characteristic is sin as socially and spiritually contagious, mediated through authority.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The sinning is transmitted through social/authority relationship, not chosen independently — distinguished from habitual defection (Char-R6) by the source in another person's will.  
> **Keyword family:** `leadership corrupting` (8–10 across both sub-groups), `defection transmitted` (6 in M10-B, 3 co-occ with `sin contagious`), `sin contagious`, `contagion moral`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~32V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A primary (Jeroboam pattern), some M10-B  
> **Sample anchors:** 1Ki 14:16 (Jeroboam drew whole nation into sin), 1Ki 16:2 (charged with misusing authority to lead Israel into sin), 2Ki 17:21 (Jeroboam drove them from the Lord), Jer 32:35 (caused by corrupting leadership into child sacrifice), 2Pe 2:14 (enticing unstable souls — contagious inner corruption)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R8 — Political revolt as sinful act
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Breaking submission to established authority — the wilful act of a subordinate people or person asserting independence against a governing relationship; in Scripture's moral vocabulary, this defection carries the weight of sinful transgression.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The sin is specifically political-relational defection — authority relationship broken; distinct from covenant-betrayal (M10-G) by the political rather than covenantal frame.  
> **Keyword family:** `defection political` (3 co-occ with `authority rejected`, `submission broken`), `authority rejected` (3), `submission broken` (3), `loyalty severed`, `independence asserting`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** 9V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A (pa.sha secondary allocation — 9 verses only)  
> **Sample anchors:** 1Ki 12:19 (Israel's ongoing rebellion against Davidic house), 2Ki 1:1 (Moab breaks political submission), 2Ki 8:20 (Edom revolts from Judah)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R9 — Sinful speech: blasphemy and slander (M06 cross-register)
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin committed through the mouth directed against God or persons — verbal acts that originate in inner moral corruption (heart-generated: Mat 15:19; Mar 7:22) and express themselves as slander, contemptuous assertion, or blasphemous presumption.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The instrument of the sinful act is speech; the source is inner moral corruption or hostility.  
> **Keyword family:** `corruption verbal` (5 in M10-H but present in M10-A blasfēmia terms), `speech perverted` (3 co-occ with `corruption verbal`)  
> **Cross-register:** M06 (Hate, Contempt and Hostility) preserved throughout  
> **Estimated verse volume:** 22V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A (blasfēmia 18V + blasfēmos 4V)  
> **Sample anchors:** Mat 15:19 (slander originates in the heart), Mar 7:22 (inner-generated evil), Joh 10:33 (blasphemy as presumptuous claim to divinity), Rev 13:6 (comprehensive verbal assault from the will)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R10 — Enticement, hypocrisy, apostasy: specialised sinful mechanisms (M14/M08/M31 cross-register)
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin committed through a specific inner mechanism — desire exploited by enticement (deleazō: the desire-hook), identity falsified through performed hypocrisy (sunupokrinomai), or covenantal identity abandoned through apostasy (apostasia).  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The sin operates through a specific inner faculty or mechanism rather than direct willing.  
> **Keyword family:** (small corpus; mechanism-specific)  
> **Cross-register:** M14 (deleazō), M08 (sunupokrinomai), M31 (apostasia)  
> **Estimated verse volume:** 5V  
> **Source pool:** M10-A small-corpus terms  
> **Sample anchors:** Jam 1:14 (desire as internal hook), 2Pe 2:14 (insatiable desire bent to lure others), Gal 2:13 (hypocrisy as social moral contagion), Act 21:21 (apostasy as covenantal defection)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R11 — Sin as moral condition: the universal human state
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin as a structural condition of the inner person — not primarily what they did but what they are under: every person is under sin's dominion, subject to it as a power, fallen short of the glory that was humanity's intended end.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Not the act of sinning but the condition of being a sinner; the universality of the state rather than individual acts.  
> **Keyword family:** `sin condition` (6 in M10-B), `universality sin` (from hamartanō keywords), `guilt personal` (8 in M10-B) — especially verses framing sin as the shared human problem  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~50V  
> **Source pool:** M10-B primary (hamartia universal passages; chat.tat condition-state passages)  
> **Sample anchors:** Rom 3:23 (all have sinned, fall short of glory), Rom 5:12 (sin entered the world, spread to all), 1Ki 8:46 (no one who does not sin), Joh 8:34 (practicing sin makes one sin's slave), Eph 2:1 (dead in trespasses — condition not act)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R12 — Sin as enslaving power: bondage of the will
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin as an active force or power that masters the inner person, governing the will so that the person cannot freely choose otherwise — the will captive under sin's dominion.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Agency is compromised — the will is not free but enslaved; distinct from the universal condition (Char-R11) by the specific bondage-of-will element.  
> **Keyword family:** `sin condition` paired with `will clinging`, `departure refused` (in M10-B: 7 instances of `departure refused`), `will persisting`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~30V  
> **Source pool:** M10-B primary  
> **Sample anchors:** Joh 8:34 (practicing sin makes one its slave — will enslaved), Gen 4:7 (sin crouching at the door, its desire for you — predatory power), Rom 6:14/15 (no longer under sin's dominion), Gal 5:1 (do not return to yoke of slavery), 1Jo 3:9 (divine birth makes sustained sinning structurally incompatible)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R13 — Sin as burden: recorded weight before God
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin as an objective moral weight existing before God — recorded, accumulated, not hidden from divine memory even if hidden from others; the inner person carries this record whether they feel it or not.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The weight exists in God's reckoning, not primarily in the conscience — distinct from guilt-as-felt-weight (M10-D) by its objective divine-record dimension.  
> **Keyword family:** `sin recorded` (5 in M10-B), `sin accumulating` (6), `guilt accumulating` (4), `memory divine` (13 cluster-wide, concentrated in M10-B), `record divine` (8), `sin named`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~45V  
> **Source pool:** M10-B primary (chat.tat burden-of-sin passages; hamartia record passages)  
> **Sample anchors:** Exo 32:32–34 (sin recorded, God will visit it on its appointed day), Rev 18:5 (her sins heaped to heaven — divine record at capacity), Gen 4:7 (sin crouching, its record awaiting), Lev 16:21 (all sins of Israel verbally named and transferred), Num 32:23 (your sin will find you out — record produces consequence)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R14 — Forgiveness sought and received: the sin-response of seeking pardon
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** The inner movement toward God in search of forgiveness — the will that turns and asks for sin's removal; and the divine response of granting, withholding, or declaring forgiveness. The characteristic is the inner act of seeking pardon and/or the experience of receiving it.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** Directed toward the resolution of sin — distinct from confession (Char-R3, which names the sin) by the additional element of appealing to God for its removal.  
> **Keyword family:** `forgiveness sought` (11 in M10-B, 9 cluster-lead), `pardon sought` (11), `forgiveness received` (14 cluster-wide), `forgiveness divine` (8), `burden lifted` (6), `guilt removed` (6), `guilt released`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~55V  
> **Source pool:** M10-B primary (hamartia forgiveness passages; chat.tat atonement-associated passages; kip.pu.rim; chat.tat sin-offering)  
> **Cross-register:** M11 (Repentance, Forgiveness, Restoration) for kip.pu.rim (8V) and chat.tat sin-offering (4V)  
> **Sample anchors:** Psa 51:1–2 (have mercy, blot out transgressions), Luk 7:47–48 (forgiven much, sin declared removed), 1Jo 1:9 (if we confess, faithful and just to forgive), Exo 30:16 (atonement money covering moral debt), Lev 16:34 (annual atonement for all Israel's sins)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R15 — Sin inherited and transmitted: the generational moral condition
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** Sin as a moral condition that enters through lineage — inherited from ancestors, transmitted through family or national belonging; the inner person carries a guilt or moral liability not only for their own acts but for the accumulated sinful history of those before them.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The source of the sin-condition is generational transmission — distinct from personal sin-as-condition (Char-R11) by its intergenerational origin.  
> **Keyword family:** `guilt inherited` (10), `iniquity inherited` (7), `defection generational` (8), `guilt transmitted` (13 cluster-wide), `defection transmitted` (6 in M10-B), `sin inherited` (7), `iniquity generational`  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~40V  
> **Source pool:** M10-B primary; overlap with M10-A (Jeroboam transmitted pattern is Char-R7)  
> **Sample anchors:** Lam 5:7 (fathers sinned and are gone, present generation bears their iniquities), Exo 20:5 (iniquity of fathers visited on children to third and fourth generation), Lev 26:39 (wasting away in the iniquity of their fathers), Jer 3:25 (sinning from youth spanning generations), Dan 9:8 (shame belonging to kings, princes, and fathers alike)
> 
> ---
> 
> ### Char-R16 — Wilful persistence in sin despite turning known
> 
> **Inner-being operation:** The inner state of refusing to release sin even while its wrongness is known — the will that clings to its sinful course after having been confronted with the requirement to turn; characterised by an active, chosen self-hardening. This is the obdurate will, not ignorant but entrenched.  
> **Distinguishing feature:** The person knows the call to repent and actively resists it — distinct from refusal-to-repent (Char-R5, which is the act of withholding turning) by focusing on the sustained inner state of the entrenched will under confrontation.  
> **Keyword family:** `departure refused` + `sin inherited` (4 co-occ), `conscience suppressed`, `will clinging` (3 co-occ with `departure refused`), `sin persisting` + `turning withheld`, `departure refused` + `turning withheld` (6 co-occ)  
> **Estimated verse volume:** ~30V  
> **Source pool:** M10-B primary (chat.tat persistence passages); some M10-A  
> **Sample anchors:** 1Ki 8:46–47 (sinning and then confessing in exile — the sequence of sin and eventual turning), Neh 9:29 (stubborn shoulder, stiff neck — sinning against God's rules), Eze 33:12 (decisive act of sin that overrides prior righteousness), Jer 8:14 (sinning against God recognized only in consequence)
> 
> ---

#### obs #164 — M10 sub-group design REVISION — §2. Revised sub-group design

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design_revision
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5 b/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-revision-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> Revised sub-group codes retain the M10 prefix with new letter codes. M10-A and M10-B are subdivided; their old codes are retired and replaced.
> 
> | New code | Label | From | Est. verses | Characteristic |
> |---|---|---:|---:|---|
> | M10-J | Wilful sinning | M10-A | ~55 | Char-R1 |
> | M10-K | Unintentional sinning | M10-A | ~32 | Char-R2 |
> | M10-L | Confession: conscience naming sin | M10-A | ~42 | Char-R3 |
> | M10-M | Conscience suppression and self-deception | M10-A/B | ~28 | Char-R4 |
> | M10-N | Refusal to repent | M10-A/B | ~35 | Char-R5 |
> | M10-O | Habitual defection | M10-A/B | ~30 | Char-R6 |
> | M10-P | Contagious sin: leadership transmission | M10-A/B | ~32 | Char-R7 |
> | M10-Q | Political revolt as sinful act | M10-A | 9 | Char-R8 |
> | M10-R | Sinful speech: blasphemy and slander | M10-A | 22 | Char-R9 (M06) |
> | M10-S | Enticement, hypocrisy, apostasy | M10-A | 5 | Char-R10 (M14/M08/M31) |
> | M10-T | Sin as universal human condition | M10-B | ~50 | Char-R11 |
> | M10-U | Sin as enslaving power | M10-B | ~30 | Char-R12 |
> | M10-V | Sin as burden: divine record | M10-B | ~45 | Char-R13 |
> | M10-W | Forgiveness sought and received | M10-B | ~55 | Char-R14 (M11) |
> | M10-X | Generational sin inheritance | M10-A/B | ~40 | Char-R15 |
> | M10-Y | Wilful persistence despite confrontation | M10-B | ~30 | Char-R16 |
> 
> **Total revised estimate:** 55+32+42+28+35+30+32+9+22+5+50+30+45+55+40+30 = **540V across 16 sub-groups**
> 
> *Note: Estimated total exceeds 613 because several verses carry characteristics that overlap two adjacent clusters (e.g. a verse evidencing both confession and guilt-surfacing). These will resolve cleanly at the per-verse mapping stage below. The overlap is in estimates, not in assignments — each verse routes to exactly one sub-group.*
> 
> **Revised estimate reconciled to 613V:**
> 
> | Code | Revised est. |
> |---|---:|
> | M10-J | 50 |
> | M10-K | 30 |
> | M10-L | 38 |
> | M10-M | 22 |
> | M10-N | 32 |
> | M10-O | 28 |
> | M10-P | 30 |
> | M10-Q | 9 |
> | M10-R | 22 |
> | M10-S | 5 |
> | M10-T | 48 |
> | M10-U | 35 |
> | M10-V | 50 |
> | M10-W | 65 |
> | M10-X | 40 |
> | M10-Y | 29 |
> | **Total** | **533** |
> 
> *Remaining ~80V will be allocated by the per-verse mapping (§3) as small verses across these sub-groups that were not captured in the initial estimates. The distribution check (§4) confirms no sub-group approaches 530V.*
> 
> ---

#### obs #165 — M10 sub-group design REVISION — §3. Term-to-sub-group remap (M10-A + M10-B verses only)

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_5_subgroup_design_revision
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/files phase 5 b/wa-cluster-M10-subgroup-design-revision-v1-20260523.md`

**description:**

> This section provides the term-level routing rules. CC's Phase 6 partial-redo script applies these rules, with per-verse exceptions listed explicitly.
> 
> ### Term-level routing rules
> 
> **cha.ta H2398 (201V — all from M10-A):**
> 
> Primary split by keyword pattern:
> 
> - **Deliberate wilful sinning** (sin-against-God named as personal defection, not ritual) → M10-J
>   - Includes: Gen 39:9, Jos 7:20, Exo 32:31/33, 2Sa 12:13, Dan 9:5/8/11/15, 1Sa 15:24, Eze 18:4/20/24, Psa 51:4, Jer 14:7, Jer 50:14, Hos 4:7, Mic 7:9, Isa 42:24, 2Ki 17:7, Jer 33:8, Jer 44:23, Eze 14:13, Jer 40:3
> 
> - **Unintentional sinning / cultic-ritual** (Lev 4–6 block; Num 15; altar-purification) → M10-K
>   - Includes: Lev 4:2/3/14/22/23/27/28/35, Lev 5:1/5/6/7/10/11/13/15/16/17, Lev 6:2/3/4/26, Lev 8:15, Lev 9:15, Lev 19:22, Num 15:27/28, Exo 29:36, Eze 43:20/22/23, Eze 45:18, Num 22:34, 1Sa 14:33/34
> 
> - **Confession / conscience naming** → M10-L
>   - Includes: Exo 9:27/10:16, Exo 32:30, Num 12:11, Num 21:7, Deu 1:41, 1Sa 7:6, 1Sa 12:10, 1Sa 15:30, 1Sa 26:21, 2Sa 19:20, 2Sa 24:10/17, 1Ch 21:8/17, 2Ki 18:14, Neh 1:6, Job 33:27, Dan 9:5 (partially confession register — route here; remove from M10-J), Lam 5:7 (partial confession/inheritance)
> 
> - **Refusal to repent / departure withheld** → M10-N
>   - Includes: 2Ki 3:3, 2Ki 10:29/31, 2Ki 13:2/6/11, 2Ki 14:24, 2Ki 15:9/18/24/28, Neh 9:29, Hos 8:11, Hos 10:9, Eze 33:12
> 
> - **Habitual defection / escalating pattern** → M10-O
>   - Includes: Hos 13:2, 1Ki 8:46, Ecc 7:20, Ecc 8:12, Ecc 7:26, 1Sa 2:25, Exo 9:34, 1Sa 15:24 (Saul fear-based — also partial wilful; route M10-J)
> 
> - **Leadership contagion** → M10-P
>   - Includes: 1Ki 14:16/22, 1Ki 15:26/30/34, 1Ki 16:2/13/19/26, 1Ki 21:22, 1Ki 22:52, 2Ki 17:21, 2Ki 21:11/16/17, 2Ki 23:15, Jer 32:35
> 
> - **Conscience suppression/self-deception** → M10-M
>   - Includes: Jer 2:35, Jer 16:10, Ecc 9:2, Ecc 2:26, Job 35:6
> 
> - **Sin-consequences / sin-as-burden register within cha.ta** → M10-V (burden/record)
>   - Includes: Exo 32:33 (blotted from book — divine record), Num 32:23 (sin will find you out), Lam 1:8/5:16, Psa 51:7 (sin as impurity requiring cleansing)
> 
> - **Generational / ancestral sinning** → M10-X
>   - Includes: Isa 43:27 (first father set ancestral pattern), Lam 5:7 (fathers sinned; present bears), Jer 3:25 (sinning from youth), Jer 14:20 (alongside inherited iniquity), Isa 65:20, 1Ki 8:47 (exiles' confession of inherited pattern), 2Ki 15:9/38 (generational)
> 
> - **Interpersonal / sin-against-neighbour** → M10-J (wilful sinning register; relational category within it)
>   - Includes: Gen 20:9, 1Sa 19:4/5, 1Ki 8:31, Jer 37:18, Lev 6:2/3 (moved to M10-K unintentional if neighbour-breach-as-ritual; retain in M10-J if deliberate)
> 
> - **Accountability / innocence / negation** → M10-L (conscience/naming register)
>   - Includes: Job 1:22, Job 2:10, Job 7:20, Job 31:30, Judg 11:27, Judg 20:16, Job 35:6 (moved to M10-M), Gen 31:39, Gen 43:9/44:32, 1Sa 24:11, Act 25:8
> 
> - **Universal sinning** → M10-T
>   - Includes: 1Ki 8:46 (→ M10-T), Ecc 7:20 (→ M10-T), Ecc 9:2 (both M10-M and M10-T; route M10-T as primary), Isa 64:5 (all sinned), Ecc 7:26
> 
> ---
> 
> **hamartanō G0264 (37V — all from M10-A):**
> 
> - **Wilful / deliberate sinning acts** → M10-J: Gen 39:9 (already cha.ta), Joh 5:14, Joh 8:11, Act 25:8, Heb 10:26, 1Pe 2:20, 2Pe 2:4
> - **Interpersonal sinning** → M10-J: Mat 18:15/21, Luk 17:3/4, 1Cor 8:12
> - **Universal sinning** → M10-T: Rom 2:12, Rom 3:23, Rom 5:12/14/16, 1Cor 7:28/36 (negation: marriage not sin — conscience/freedom register → M10-L)
> - **Confession / conscience** → M10-L: Mat 27:4, Luk 15:18/21, 1Jo 1:10
> - **Refusal / habitual** → M10-N or M10-O: Heb 3:17 (wilderness — habitual → M10-O), 1Ti 5:20 (entrenched will → M10-N), Tit 3:11 (self-condemned → M10-M)
> - **Conscience suppression** → M10-M: 1Jo 1:10 (denying sinfulness), 1Cor 15:34 (ongoing sinning + ignorance of God)
> - **New-birth / sin prevented** → M10-U (enslaving power / liberation): 1Jo 3:6/8/9/18, Eph 4:26, Rom 6:15
> - **Consequences** → M10-V: Luk 15:18 (if also confession → M10-L as primary)
> 
> ---
> 
> **blasfēmia G0988 (18V) + blasfēmos G0989 (4V):** All → M10-R
> 
> **pa.sha H6586 (political-revolt 9V):** All 9 → M10-Q
> 
> **deleazō G1185 (3V), sunupokrinomai G4942 (1V), apostasia G0646 (1V):** All 5 → M10-S
> 
> ---
> 
> **chat.tat H2403B (159V — all from M10-B) — primary routing:**
> 
> - **Sin recorded / accumulated / objective reality** → M10-V: Exo 32:32/34, Gen 4:7 (crouching predatory force), Lev 16:21 (all sins named and transferred), Lev 16:34 (recurring annual reality), 1Ki 16:31 (persistent king-pattern accumulated), Exo 34:9 (collective stubbornness + sin acknowledged)
> - **Forgiveness sought / atonement** → M10-W: Lev 4:3/14/26/28/35, Lev 5:6/10/13, Lev 10:17/19, Lev 16:16/30, Lev 19:22 (already M10-K; if in B → M10-W)
> - **Refusal / departure withheld** → M10-N: all "did not depart" (1Ki 16:31; chat.tat persistence passages)
> - **Generational / inherited** → M10-X: Lev 26:39 (wasting away in iniquity of fathers), Num 14:18 (generational consequence of sin)
> - **Sin as enslaving / condition** → M10-T or M10-U: verses showing sin as a binding reality
> 
> ---
> 
> **hamartia G0266 (105V — all from M10-B):**
> 
> - **Universal human condition** → M10-T: Joh 8:21/24 (sin as death-state), Rom 3:9 (all under sin), Rom 5:8/19 (while sinners / constituted sinners), Mat 1:21 (save from sins — condition requiring rescue)
> - **Enslaving power / bondage** → M10-U: Joh 8:34 (practicing sin = slave to sin), Rom 6:1/2/6/7/11/12/13/14 (no longer enslaved to sin — liberation framing implies prior bondage)
> - **Burden / record** → M10-V: Joh 1:29 (takes away sin of world — burden requiring removal), 1Pe 2:24 (he bore our sins), Heb 9:26/28 (put away sin — record cleared)
> - **Forgiveness / removal** → M10-W: Luk 7:47/48, Col 1:14, Eph 1:7, Mat 26:28, 1Jo 1:7, Heb 10:12
> - **Conscience / guilt** → M10-D territory (already in M10-D via a.sham family; hamartia verses touching guilt-awareness → M10-L if confession-register)
> - **Wilful sinning** → M10-J: Heb 12:1 (sin that so easily entangles — wilful clinging)
> 
> ---
> 
> **paraptōma G3900 (14V — split: 5 → M10-F already; 9 remain in M10-B):**
> - Condition / death-state (Eph 2:1/5; Col 2:13) → M10-T
> - Forgiveness / justification (Eph 1:7; Col 2:13; 2Cor 5:19) → M10-W
> - Sin real requiring grace (Gal 6:1) → M10-J
> 
> **chat.tat H2403A (2V) + cha.ta.ah H2401 (8V):** → M10-V (sin as objective named reality requiring atonement) or M10-W (forgiveness/pardon sought)
> 
> **chat.tat H2403H sin-offering (4V):** → M10-W (M11 cross-register preserved)
> 
> **chat.tat H2403I sin-punishment (2V):** → M10-V (burden/record: punishment-sense of the sin-weight)
> 
> **kip.pu.rim H3725 (8V):** → M10-W (M11 cross-register preserved)
> 
> **chet H2399 (33V):** Primary → M10-V (sin as personal liability/record before God) with ~8V to M10-J (deliberate culpable acts)
> 
> **rish.ah H7564 (4V):** → M10-T (wickedness as enduring inner condition)
> 
> **al.vah H5932 (1V):** → M10-T (iniquity-at-Gibeah as defining moral condition)
>
