### TIER_READING_GUIDE (27)

#### obs #38 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T0 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T0 is the theological ground tier for M10. Before reading any characteristic-level data in T0, Session C must hold one orienting finding: every M10 characteristic defines God's character by negation and contrast. God's holiness, mercy, patience, moral omniscience, faithfulness, and justice are each illuminated across T0 by what sin does against them. This means T0 does not primarily describe sin — it describes God. Sin is the darkness that makes God's light visible. Session C should read T0 not as background theology but as the active frame within which every window on sin is set. No chapter on sin should be written without first establishing whose character the sin is defined against.

#### obs #39 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T0 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T0.2.1 returns S (silent on positive created purpose) for all 22 characteristics without exception. This is the single most consistent finding in the entire tier. Session C should not imply that sin serves any purpose in the reader's formation, development, or journey. It has no designed function. It equips nothing, enables nothing, fulfils nothing. It is purely a departure from design. This boundary should be held clearly in every chapter: sin is not a stage in a journey toward maturity; it is the interruption of that journey.

#### obs #40 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T0 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T0.3.1 shows that every M10 characteristic operates by perverting an image-capacity rather than eliminating it. The will that sins is the same will that can confess and turn. The speech that blasphemes is the same speech designed to praise. The authority that transmits sin is the same authority designed to form community toward God. Session C should use this finding consistently: sin is serious precisely because it is the image's own capacities turned against their design — and restoration is always possible precisely because those capacities remain present. The image is not destroyed by sin; it is perverted.

#### obs #41 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T0 reading guide #4

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T0.4.1 shows that the Christological resolution is not confined to CHAR-14 (forgiveness) but is woven through at least seven characteristics as the eschatological answer embedded in the evidence itself: CHAR-1, CHAR-3, CHAR-11, CHAR-14, CHAR-16, CHAR-19, CHAR-22. Session C should not treat the Christological thread as a concluding addition to each chapter — it is embedded in the data of each characteristic and belongs at the natural convergence point within each window.

#### obs #42 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T1 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T1 is the definitional tier — it names what each characteristic IS, how it operates, and what its structural opposite is. When Session C reads T1 across the 22 characteristics, the primary finding is the cluster's internal architecture: not all 22 are the same kind of thing. Some are acts (CHAR-1, 2, 9), some are processes (CHAR-4, 5, 6), some are conditions (CHAR-11, 12, 13), and some are constituted character states (CHAR-16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 22). Session C should read T1 as the map of these distinctions before writing any chapter — mixing act-characteristics and character-characteristics in the same chapter will produce confusion.

#### obs #43 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T1 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T1.2.3 (working descriptions) provides the most reader-accessible single-paragraph description of each characteristic. Session C should treat these as starting-point definitions for each characteristic referenced in a chapter, not as chapter headings in their own right. The working descriptions are accurate but analytical — Session C's task is to translate them into reader-facing language that carries the same precision without the programme vocabulary.

#### obs #44 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T1 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T1.3.1 (structural opposites) is essential for Session C to read before writing any chapter. Each characteristic's structural opposite is named explicitly and often carries the most vivid language in the tier. The structural opposites collectively constitute a preliminary portrait of what sin's absence looks like — which is precisely the question that needs to be answered when sin's opposite is eventually described. Session C should flag these as a resource for that future work.

#### obs #45 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T2 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T2 answers the question: where in the person does this characteristic live? The finding that matters most for Session C is this: the heart is the near-universal constitutional home of M10's characteristics. 19 of 22 characteristics locate explicitly in the heart. The three exceptions (CHAR-2, CHAR-7, CHAR-12) are analytically significant — their non-heart-location is what makes them distinctive. Session C should use T2 to establish that when Scripture talks about sin, it is talking about something that happens in the heart's deliberating, willing, knowing centre — not primarily in behaviour. Behaviour is the output; the heart is the origin.

#### obs #46 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T2 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T2.1 (spirit-level) produces one finding of unique importance: CHAR-20 (Faithlessness) is the only characteristic in M10 with an explicit spirit-level command against it — Mal 2:15/16 — "guard yourselves in your spirit, and do not be faithless." This is the only place in the cluster where the spirit (*rûaḥ*) is named as the specific level from which a sin-characteristic must be resisted. Session C should treat this as the cluster's deepest constitutional finding: faithlessness requires spirit-level vigilance, not merely behavioural restraint.

#### obs #47 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T2 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T2.8 (constitutional deposit) is the tier's most practically important section for Session C. Every characteristic leaves a deposit — in the person's character, in the divine record, in the community or generation. No deposit is described as permanently beyond divine removal. Session C should use T2.8 to establish both the seriousness of sin's entrenchment (the deposits are real and deep) and the completeness of the resolution (every deposit is removable by divine action). These two truths together constitute the pastoral core of every window.

#### obs #48 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T3 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T3 maps sin's engagement with every inner faculty: perception, cognition, memory, affect, creativity, volition, agency, moral evaluation, conscience, conscientiousness, relational capacity. When Session C reads T3, the primary orientation finding is this: the conscience is the cluster's diagnostic instrument. Every characteristic has a conscience-engagement pattern — and reading those patterns across the 22 characteristics tells the story of sin's progression more clearly than any other single data source. Session C should treat T3.9 (conscience) as the narrative spine of sin's inner-being story.

#### obs #49 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T3 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T3.9 (conscience) across all 22 characteristics reveals a three-stage trajectory that Session C should use as a structural frame: (1) conscience operational — firing, naming, producing guilt and confession; (2) conscience suppressed — present but overridden by the will; (3) conscience eliminated — non-functional, producing the shamelessness of Zep 3:5 and the animal-instinct destruction of Jude 10. The depth of sin's entrenchment in any characteristic is indexed by which stage of this trajectory the characteristic occupies. Session C should use this trajectory to show the reader how sin progresses rather than simply listing its forms.

#### obs #50 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T3 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T3.6 (volition) shows that the will is the primary faculty across virtually the entire cluster — but its role changes dramatically as sin progresses: from active agent (choosing sin) through formed disposition (habituated) to captured slave (enslaved). Session C should read T3.6 alongside T3.9 to show the will and conscience as the two primary inner-being battlegrounds of sin: conscience is the witness; will is the decision-maker. When both are compromised, the person is constitutionally constituted in sin.

#### obs #51 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T3 reading guide #4

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T3.5 (creative faculty) is silent across most characteristics — but not CHAR-21 (perversion) and CHAR-22 (injustice). Pro 6:14's "perverted heart devises evil continually" and Psa 58:2's "in your hearts you devise wrongs" name the creative-devising capacity as captured by sin in these characteristics. Session C should note that sin in its advanced forms is not passive — the perverted and unjust person is actively, creatively, and continuously wrong. This distinguishes the advanced stage from moral negligence.

#### obs #52 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T4 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T4 is the relational tier — it maps sin as a relational event between the person and God, between persons, and within the spiritual landscape. The single most important reading guide for Session C is this: every characteristic's God-to-human response operates from two simultaneous poles — holiness that cannot ignore the sin, and steadfast love that keeps the relationship accessible. Neither pole cancels the other. Session C must hold both in every chapter. A chapter that presents only God's holiness produces despair; a chapter that presents only steadfast love produces presumption. The data demands both together.

#### obs #53 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T4 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T4.2.1 shows that sin disrupts the human-to-God directional movement in three distinct ways: as anti-movement (the sinning act IS movement against God — Psa 51:4), as movement-blocker (preventing the approach to God), and as movement-reverser (redirecting away from God toward false objects). Session C should use this distinction to differentiate chapters: wilful sinning and sinful speech are anti-movement; conscience suppression and refusal to repent are movement-blockers; habitual defection and faithlessness are movement-reversers. The pastoral implication differs in each case.

#### obs #54 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T4 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T4.4.3 (inner state when the characteristic is addressed) is the most positive data in the entire M10 dataset. The resolved state is not the absence of sin — it is the positive reconstitution of the person: blessedness, life, fitness for commission, teaching capacity, Spirit-indwelling, participation in divine nature, new self in God's likeness, restored covenant identity. Session C should read T4.4.3 as the destination toward which every chapter should point. The resolved state is not an afterthought — it is what the entire cluster is moving toward.

#### obs #55 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T4 reading guide #4

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T4.6 (spiritual beings) shows that adversarial spiritual involvement clusters at the structural level of sin — CHAR-11 (universal condition) and CHAR-12 (enslaving power) — rather than at the episodic level of individual sinning acts. Session C should use this finding carefully: not every sinning act involves direct adversarial engagement, but every sinner is operating within a domain that adversarial power has constituted. The distinction prevents both dismissal (pretending sin has no spiritual dimension) and overstatement (attributing every sinning act to demonic activity).

#### obs #56 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T5 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T5 is the progression tier — it maps how sin moves through the person over time. The primary reading guide for Session C is this: every characteristic has a two-way sequence — a downward arc (deeper entrenchment) and a reversal arc (the way out). Without exception across all 22 characteristics. Session C should use both arcs in every chapter. The data is never purely bleak because the reversal is embedded in the same evidence as the descent. This is not pastoral optimism added to grim data — it is what the data itself shows.

#### obs #57 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T5 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T5.2.1 (sequence of inner states) across all 22 characteristics reveals a consistent three-stage progression that Session C can use as a structural frame for the cluster's narrative: Act (CHAR-1, 2, 9, 10) → Trajectory (CHAR-4, 5, 6, 7, 11, 12, 13) → Character (CHAR-16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 22). The act becomes a habit; the habit becomes a disposition; the disposition becomes the person's moral identity. Session C should present this progression not as a mechanical inevitability but as what the data consistently evidences when sin is not addressed.

#### obs #58 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T5 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T5.6 (eschatological orientation) shows that every characteristic points toward a binary eschatological horizon: unaddressed sin moves toward judgment; addressed sin moves toward life and restoration. The language is consistent across the cluster: "he shall surely live" (Eze 33:15), "I will remember their sin no more" (Jer 31:34), "the creation itself will be set free from its bondage to corruption" (Rom 8:21). Session C should use this eschatological framing not as a chapter ending but as the horizon that gives every chapter its forward orientation — what the present state of sin is moving toward, in both directions.

#### obs #59 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T6 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T6 maps how the 22 characteristics relate to each other — which ones co-occur, which precede which, which produce which. The primary reading guide for Session C is the set of functional descriptions T6.1.2 produced for each characteristic: "the subjective-experiential face," "the objective-accumulation face," "the volitional act-face," "the relational-covenantal face," "the resolution characteristic." Session C should use these as the vocabulary for explaining to a reader why multiple characteristics are being discussed in the same chapter — they are different faces of the same reality.

#### obs #60 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T6 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T6 confirms four natural groupings that Session C can use as chapter-scope guides:
> - **Entry cluster**: CHAR-1, 2, 9, 10 — how sin enters
> - **Trajectory cluster**: CHAR-4, 5, 6, 7 — how sin deepens (tightly adjacent triad: CHAR-4 ↔ 5 ↔ 6)
> - **Condition cluster**: CHAR-11, 12, 13, 15 — the structural conditions of sin's existence
> - **Character cluster**: CHAR-16, 17, 18, 19, 20, 21, 22 — what the person becomes
> - **Resolution**: CHAR-3, 14 — the exit characteristics
> Session C does not need to write one chapter per characteristic. These groupings can constitute the chapter architecture.

#### obs #61 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T6 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T6.5.2 (boundary-case verses) identifies the verses that straddle two characteristics and belong at the joints between chapters rather than inside any one: Psa 51:3 (CHAR-13/17), Psa 58:2 (CHAR-21/22), Hos 6:7 (CHAR-19/20), Hos 13:12 (CHAR-18/13), Exo 34:7 (CHAR-18/19/1). Session C should use these boundary verses as transition passages between chapters — they are the cluster's own joints, showing how one window flows into the next.

#### obs #62 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T7 reading guide #1

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T7.1 (vocabulary arc) provides a resource Session C should use selectively rather than exhaustively. The primary reading guide: each characteristic's vocabulary arc traces the OT-to-NT development of the concept. Some characteristics are exclusively OT Hebrew (CHAR-17, 18, 20 — no NT vocabulary); some are primarily NT Greek (CHAR-12); most span both. Session C should use the vocabulary arc to establish the characteristic's linguistic roots before translating it into reader-facing language — the etymology often carries the most vivid and precise image of what the characteristic IS.

#### obs #63 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T7 reading guide #2

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T7.3 (human science frameworks) is the tier's most directly useful resource for Session C's reader-facing writing. The finding that applies across the entire cluster: science illuminates the horizontal dimensions of sin (mechanism, social dynamics, psychological formation, institutional consequences) with considerable precision, and diverges from the data at the vertical dimension — the relational reality before God. Session C should use T7.3 to show the reader that their lived experience of sin's mechanisms (conscience suppression, habit formation, addiction-like bonding, institutional corruption) is recognised and named by the data — before adding the vertical dimension that science cannot supply.

#### obs #64 — M10 Phase 9 — Tier T7 reading guide #3

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_9_synthesis
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-cluster-M10-phase9-synthesis-findings-v1-20260524.md`

**description:**

> T7.3.3 (divergences between science and verse evidence) is the most important sub-section for Session C's use. The divergence falls at the same structural point across all 22 characteristics: science describes sin's horizontal effects; the biblical data adds what sin does before God — and what God does in response. Session C should use this divergence as a bridge to the reader who may engage with the horizontal reality before accepting the vertical. Start where the reader is (the recognisable human experience); move to where the data goes (the vertical relational reality that constitutes sin as sin).

#### obs #215 — M10 Phase 3 STAYS — H2398 cha.ta (to sin)

- **status:** open  ·  **target_phase:** session_c  ·  **source_phase:** phase_3_constitution_debate
- **source_file:** `Sessions/Session_Clusters/M10/wa-m10-phase3-constitution-verdicts-v1-20260522.md`

**description:**

> **Rationale:** 201 meanings form the densest OT sin-act corpus. Covers sinning as directed against God (Gen 39:9; Exo 32:30; 2Sa 12:13), against specific persons (Gen 42:22; 1Sa 19:4/5), as wilful pattern (1Ki 14:16; 2Ki 3:3), as conscience-struck act (2Sa 24:10), and as universal condition (1Ki 8:46). Core M10.
> 
> ---
> 
> ### H2399 chet — sin — STAYS
> *(mti_id not confirmed in §2; corpus verification requested from CC)*
> 
> **Rationale:** Primary Hebrew sin noun. Corpus-identity inference: term appears in cluster gloss list; corpus content would be sin-act/state vocabulary consistent with M10. **Flag to CC:** verify mti_id and verse count for H2399 chet; confirm §2 entry exists in constitution report.
>

## §8. Pass A meanings + keywords (verse_context, is_relevant=1)

Per-verse meaning + atomic keywords from Pass A. Grouped by sub-group → VCG → canonical order.

**Total meanings:** 1320

### M10-C

#### M10-C-VCG-01 (30 verses)

- **vc=19168** 1Ki 1:21 `H2400 chat.ta`: Bathsheba fears she and Solomon will be 'counted offenders' if Adonijah takes the throne, showing that sinner/offender is a social-legal status that can be assigned by those in power, carrying life-threatening consequences. — keywords: `status assigned`, `offender labeled`, `guilt imputed`, `identity threatened`, `social condemnation`
- **vc=19169** Psa 1:1 `H2400 chat.ta`: The blessed man avoids standing in the way of sinners, treating sinners as a social-moral class whose path and company exert a gravitational pull that shapes inner orientation and conduct. — keywords: `influence contagious`, `path moral`, `company gravitational`, `orientation shaped`, `will resisting`, `contamination social`
- **vc=19170** Psa 1:5 `H2400 chat.ta`: Sinners are excluded from the congregation of the righteous at judgment, showing their identity as those whose inner moral character bars them from standing before God and the upright community. — keywords: `exclusion judgment`, `identity disqualifying`, `standing forfeited`, `character bars`, `community righteous denied`
- **vc=19171** Psa 25:8 `H2400 chat.ta`: Sinners are not abandoned but are the objects of God's instruction in the way, showing the sinner's inner condition as one of lostness or moral disorientation that can be redirected by divine teaching. — keywords: `lostness moral`, `disorientation inner`, `instruction divine`, `redirecting`, `teachable potential`, `return enabled`
- **vc=19172** Psa 26:9 `H2400 chat.ta`: Sinners are those whose company is deadly to the soul; the psalmist fears being swept away with them, framing the sinner's character as a destructive communal identity that endangers even the innocent bystander. — keywords: `contamination feared`, `identity dangerous`, `soul imperiled`, `association deadly`, `separation sought`
- **vc=18779** Mat 9:10 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Sinners are a recognized social and moral category who gather around Jesus at table—their association with tax collectors marks them as those whose inner moral standing excludes them from respectable society but not from Jesus. — keywords: `exclusion social`, `marginalization moral`, `belonging sought`, `reception unexpected`, `identity stigmatized`
- **vc=18780** Mat 9:11 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The Pharisees use 'sinners' as a social-moral label marking people whose inner character is seen as defiled, making table fellowship with them scandalous in their view. — keywords: `label social`, `defilement perceived`, `scandal religious`, `stigma moral`, `separation enforced`, `judgment external`
- **vc=18781** Mat 9:13 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Jesus identifies sinners as those who need his call, contrasting them with the self-styled righteous; their inner condition is one of need rather than self-sufficiency. — keywords: `need inner`, `self-sufficiency absent`, `call received`, `mercy needed`, `receptivity`, `condition needy`
- **vc=18782** Mat 11:19 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Jesus is labeled a friend of sinners by critics who view such association as morally compromising; sinners here are those whose lifestyle disqualifies them from respectable standing. — keywords: `association stigmatized`, `label accusatory`, `lifestyle disqualifying`, `criticism external`, `friendship redemptive`
- **vc=18784** Mar 2:15 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Sinners are those who recline with Jesus at table — socially and morally marginalized people whose inner condition is viewed by the religious establishment as disqualifying for association with the holy. — keywords: `marginalization social`, `identity disqualifying`, `belonging unexpected`, `following drawn`, `holiness perceived threat`, `reception scandalous`
- **vc=18785** Mar 2:16 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The scribes of the Pharisees view eating with sinners as morally contaminating, treating their sinful status as an inner-character defect that should be avoided rather than engaged. — keywords: `contamination moral`, `avoidance stigma`, `character defect`, `othering judgment`, `purity calculus`
- **vc=18786** Mar 2:17 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Jesus likens sinners to the sick who need a physician, framing their sinful condition as an inner moral illness that he has come specifically to address and heal. — keywords: `moral illness`, `need interior`, `healing reception`, `unworthiness recognized`, `condition addressed`
- **vc=18789** Luk 5:8 `G0268 hamartōlos` ★: Peter's confession — 'I am a sinful man' — is a spontaneous inner recognition of his own moral unworthiness in the presence of Jesus' divine power, driving him to prostrate himself in awe. — keywords: `conscience strike`, `unworthiness surfacing`, `awe overwhelming`, `self-recognition spontaneous`, `prostration inner`, `guilt surfacing`
- **vc=18790** Luk 5:30 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Pharisees object to Jesus eating with sinners, treating such persons' moral status as a contaminant that disqualifies them from shared table fellowship with the religiously observant. — keywords: `contamination feared`, `purity calculus`, `exclusion social`, `judgment external`, `stigma moral`
- **vc=18791** Luk 5:32 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Jesus explicitly names sinners — not the self-righteous — as his target audience, framing their sinful condition as the very need that draws him and the ground for calling them to repentance. — keywords: `repentance called`, `need moral`, `condition targeted`, `turning invited`, `sinfulness ground`
- **vc=18795** Luk 7:34 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Critics use 'friend of sinners' as a slur against Jesus, treating the sinful person's inner moral condition as something that morally contaminates those who associate with them. — keywords: `contamination feared`, `association stigma`, `purity calculus`, `judgment external`, `othering social`
- **vc=18796** Luk 7:37 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The woman is identified by the city as 'a sinner,' a known moral status that defines her public identity and makes her approach to Jesus in a Pharisee's house socially scandalous. — keywords: `identity stigmatized`, `status public`, `boldness unexpected`, `approach courageous`, `shame overridden`
- **vc=18797** Luk 7:39 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The Pharisee privately concludes that a prophet would know this woman is a sinner and therefore refuse her touch; her sinful inner character is seen as a moral contagion a holy man should detect and avoid. — keywords: `contamination moral`, `inner verdict`, `purity calculus`, `detection presumed`, `avoidance expected`, `judgment private`
- **vc=18798** Luk 13:2 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Jesus challenges the assumption that greater suffering signals greater sinfulness, rejecting a direct moral-causal link between personal sin and catastrophe. — keywords: `causality assumed`, `judgment challenged`, `suffering misread`, `moral calculus rejected`, `assumption corrected`
- **vc=18799** Luk 15:1 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Those publicly classified as sinners are drawn toward Jesus to hear him, showing their inner openness to teaching despite their social-moral stigma. — keywords: `openness inner`, `receptivity drawing`, `stigma transcended`, `hunger spiritual`, `approach willing`
- **vc=18800** Luk 15:2 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The Pharisees' complaint that Jesus receives sinners and eats with them frames such persons as morally disqualified from fellowship, revealing a judgment based on perceived inner corruption. — keywords: `contamination feared`, `fellowship denied`, `judgment external`, `corruption perceived`, `exclusion moral`
- **vc=18802** Luk 18:13 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The tax collector's plea—'be merciful to me, a sinner'—shows sinfulness experienced as a deep inner unworthiness that drives him to prostrate, eyes-down prayer rather than self-justification. — keywords: `unworthiness felt`, `conscience crushing`, `plea mercy`, `self-abasement bodily`, `guilt acknowledged`, `self-justification absent`
- **vc=18803** Luk 19:7 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The crowd's grumbling that Jesus lodged with 'a sinner' treats Zacchaeus's moral status as a social and spiritual disqualification that should exclude him from honorable company. — keywords: `stigma social`, `exclusion presumed`, `status disqualifying`, `judgment crowd`, `fellowship contested`
- **vc=18805** Joh 9:16 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Some Pharisees label Jesus a sinner because he broke the Sabbath, while others question how a sinner could do such signs—sinfulness is contested as an inner status that would disqualify divine action. — keywords: `status contested`, `disqualification assumed`, `verdict divided`, `sinfulness debated`, `evidence resisted`
- **vc=18806** Joh 9:24 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The authorities declare Jesus a sinner with certainty, using that moral verdict to discredit him—inner sinfulness is treated as an established fact that negates any claim to divine authority. — keywords: `verdict imposed`, `authority denied`, `sinfulness declared`, `discrediting intent`, `certainty false`
- **vc=18807** Joh 9:25 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The healed man honestly admits he cannot determine whether Jesus is a sinner, but insists on the undeniable fact of his own healing—distinguishing inner moral status from observable effect. — keywords: `status uncertain`, `experience undeniable`, `distinction moral`, `honesty epistemic`, `knowledge limited`, `evidence personal`
- **vc=18808** Joh 9:31 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The principle stated is that God does not hear sinners but does hear worshipers who do his will—inner sinfulness cuts off the sinner from divine responsiveness, while obedience opens it. — keywords: `access divine`, `sinfulness blocking`, `obedience opening`, `prayer severed`, `responsiveness conditional`, `will divine`
- **vc=18813** Gal 2:15 `G0268 hamartōlos`: 'Gentile sinners' is used as a received ethnic-religious category that Jews applied to non-Jews, reflecting a social assumption that Gentile identity was inherently marked by a sinful standing before God. — keywords: `identity assumed`, `status ethnic`, `standing presumed`, `category social`, `otherness moral`
- **vc=18816** Heb 7:26 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Sinners represent the morally contaminated human condition from which Christ's high priesthood is entirely separated — his holiness is defined by total inner and positional distance from sinners. — keywords: `contamination moral`, `separation positional`, `holiness contrast`, `purity absolute`, `condition human`
- **vc=18820** 1Pe 4:18 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The sinner stands in contrast to the righteous who are scarcely saved — the verse implies the sinner's moral standing leaves them in far greater peril of condemnation, with no secure path through judgment. — keywords: `peril judgment`, `standing insecure`, `condemnation certain`, `contrast righteous`, `path absent`, `vulnerability moral`

#### M10-C-VCG-02 (20 verses)

- **vc=18801** Luk 15:10 `G0268 hamartōlos`: A single sinner's repentance produces joy among the angels, affirming that the inner turning of a morally wayward person has cosmic significance. — keywords: `repentance turning`, `joy cosmic`, `significance inner`, `turning celebrated`, `moral reversal`

- **vc=18809** Rom 3:7 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The sinner is one condemned even when their lie paradoxically served to magnify God's truth; being a sinner here is an inner moral status that makes one liable to judgment regardless of the outcome that flows from one's act. — keywords: `status moral`, `condemnation liability`, `guilt objective`, `deception inner`, `judgment deserved`
- **vc=18810** Rom 5:8 `G0268 hamartōlos` ★: Being a sinner is the moral condition Christ died for — 'while we were still sinners' — meaning Christ's love was demonstrated precisely when humanity was in its worst inner state, with no mitigating righteousness to commend them. — keywords: `condition unredeemed`, `righteousness absent`, `status worst`, `love unmerited`, `guilt unmitigated`
- **vc=18811** Rom 5:19 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Many were constituted sinners through one man's disobedience — not by their individual choice but by their participation in Adam — showing that being a sinner is an imputed inner status arising from a federal representative act of disobedience. — keywords: `status imputed`, `constitution sinful`, `disobedience federal`, `identity inherited`, `participation involuntary`
- **vc=18812** Rom 7:13 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Through the commandment sin becomes visible in its full, extreme sinfulness — the law serves to magnify sin's character as exceedingly corrupt, revealing its true inner nature beyond measure. — keywords: `sin exposed`, `corruption magnified`, `nature revealed`, `law revealing`, `excess sinful`, `death producing`
- **vc=18814** Gal 2:17 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Being found to be sinners while seeking justification in Christ raises the question of whether Christ enables sin — Paul's denial asserts that a sinful standing does not follow from faith-union with Christ. — keywords: `status discovered`, `justification seeking`, `union faith`, `standing questioned`, `guilt apparent`
- **vc=18815** 1Ti 1:9 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Sinners are listed among the lawless and ungodly — those whose inner moral orientation is against God's law, making them the very persons for whom the law's restraining function is designed. — keywords: `orientation anti-law`, `will lawless`, `restraint needed`, `disposition ungodly`, `conscience absent`, `defection habitual`
- **vc=18778** 1Ti 1:15 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Paul identifies himself as the foremost sinner, placing the inner weight of sinfulness entirely on himself — Christ's saving mission is directed precisely toward those who bear the greatest moral guilt. — keywords: `guilt self-owned`, `foremost sinner`, `self-knowledge moral`, `humility conscience`, `weight sinfulness`, `saving target`
- **vc=18817** Heb 12:3 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Sinners directed hostility against Christ — the verse highlights the active opposition of the sinful will, and Christ's endurance of it is offered as the inner resource against weariness and faintheartedness. — keywords: `will hostile`, `opposition active`, `endurance inner`, `weariness resisted`, `hostility directed`, `defection aggressive`
- **vc=18818** Jam 4:8 `G0268 hamartōlos`: Sinners are called to cleanse their hands while the double-minded are called to purify their hearts — the sinner's condition is externally enacted but the verse demands inner purification, linking sinfulness to a divided, unclean heart. — keywords: `heart divided`, `cleansing needed`, `double-mindedness`, `purification inner`, `distance closing`, `will returning`
- **vc=18819** Jam 5:20 `G0268 hamartōlos`: The sinner is one who has wandered from truth, heading toward death — turning such a person back rescues both soul and covers the accumulated sins, showing the sinner's state as an inner drift away from God. — keywords: `wandering inner`, `drift spiritual`, `soul endangered`, `return possible`, `sins accumulated`, `death approaching`

### M10-D

#### M10-D-VCG-01 (18 verses)

- **vc=18899** Gen 42:21 `H0818 a.shem`: The brothers recognize inner guilt as the cause of their present distress; their conscience connects their past cruelty—ignoring their brother's soul-anguish—directly to their current suffering. — keywords: `conscience surfacing`, `guilt recognized`, `causal connection`, `distress linked`, `past cruelty`, `realization delayed`
- **vc=18827** Lev 4:13 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt here arises after the congregation comes to realize what they have done; the inner recognition of guilt follows the act, suggesting conscience engages after the fact when the violation surfaces to awareness. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `unintentional violation`, `conscience delayed`, `realization post-act`, `awareness surfacing`
- **vc=18828** Lev 4:22 `H0816 a.sham`: A leader's guilt is realized after an unintentional violation; the inner moment of realization is named as the trigger for the remedial process, marking conscience as the faculty that activates accountability. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `realization triggering`, `conscience activating`, `unintentional act`, `accountability awakened`
- **vc=18829** Lev 4:27 `H0816 a.sham`: An ordinary person's guilt, like that of a leader, arises through unintentional violation and is confirmed when conscience brings realization; the guilt is real and must be addressed regardless of the lack of deliberate intent. — keywords: `guilt real`, `unintentional violation`, `conscience confirming`, `realization ordinary`, `ignorance insufficient`
- **vc=18830** Lev 5:2 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt is realized after contact with uncleanness that was initially hidden from the person; the inner realization of guilt follows discovery, showing that conscience responds when knowledge comes, even for unwitting violations. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `hiddenness lifting`, `conscience responding`, `knowledge triggering`, `unwitting contact`
- **vc=18831** Lev 5:3 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt again emerges from a hidden violation that becomes known; the moment of coming to know triggers realization of guilt, demonstrating that conscience acts upon knowledge as the bridge between the act and moral responsibility. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `knowledge bridging`, `conscience awakened`, `hidden violation`, `knowing triggering`
- **vc=18832** Lev 5:4 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt arises from a rash oath spoken with the lips, even if the implications were hidden at the time; when the person comes to know it, guilt is realized, linking the spoken word to inner moral accountability. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `rash oath`, `speech liability`, `hidden implication`, `accountability verbal`
- **vc=18826** Lev 5:5 `H0816 a.sham` ★: Guilt is the internal state recognized and then verbally confessed; realization leads to confession, showing guilt as moving from inner awareness through to the will's response of honest acknowledgment before God. — keywords: `guilt recognized`, `confession following`, `awareness verbal`, `will responding`, `acknowledgment honest`
- **vc=18833** Lev 5:17 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt here is realized even without prior knowledge of the sin; the person must bear their iniquity once awareness comes, showing that guilt is an objective moral state that exists independently of subjective awareness. — keywords: `guilt objective`, `awareness belated`, `iniquity borne`, `conscience arriving`, `sin real`
- **vc=18834** Lev 5:19 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt here is declared as an objective fact — 'he has indeed incurred guilt before the Lord' — confirming guilt as a real moral standing before God that exists regardless of the person's subjective perception of the act. — keywords: `guilt declared`, `standing objective`, `liability divine`, `subjective irrelevance`, `guilt real`
- **vc=18835** Lev 6:4 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt is realized after sinning through wrongful taking or deception; this realization in the conscience then obligates active restitution, showing guilt as an inner state that, once acknowledged, demands concrete corrective action toward the wronged party. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `conscience obligating`, `restitution demanded`, `conscience active`, `corrective action`
- **vc=18836** Num 5:6 `H0816 a.sham`: Being guilty is the inner state that follows when a person realizes they have sinned by breaking faith with God — conscience becomes the faculty through which guilt is recognized, triggering the obligation to address the wrong. — keywords: `guilt realized`, `faith broken`, `conscience recognizing`, `obligation triggered`, `awareness guilt`
- **vc=18837** Num 5:7 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt here moves outward into obligatory action — the guilty person must confess and make full restitution, showing that bearing guilt creates a moral debt on the conscience that must be discharged through tangible repair. — keywords: `guilt confessed`, `restitution obligated`, `moral debt`, `conscience discharged`, `repair tangible`
- **vc=65838** Judg 21:22 `H0816 a.sham`: Being guilty here is a moral-legal state that fathers and brothers might rightly claim against the tribe of Benjamin for taking wives without consent; the verse negotiates culpability, arguing that the unusual circumstances deflect guilt from the givers. — keywords: `guilt deflected`, `culpability negotiated`, `circumstance mitigating`, `liability avoided`, `moral accountability`
- **vc=18900** 2Sa 14:13 `H0818 a.shem`: The woman turns the king's logic back on him, showing that his refusal to restore Absalom convicts the king himself of guilt—his own judicial decision becomes the evidence of his inner moral self-condemnation. — keywords: `self-condemnation`, `conscience exposed`, `logic reversed`, `guilt surfacing`, `judgment own`, `will indicting`
- **vc=18901** Ezr 10:19 `H0818 a.shem`: Guilt here is directly tied to a remedial act — offering a ram — and to a pledge to put away foreign wives, showing guiltiness as a recognized moral state that demands both acknowledgment and costly action. — keywords: `guilt acknowledged`, `atonement costly`, `pledge remedial`, `guilt offering`, `action required`, `guilt recognized`
- **vc=18843** Psa 34:22 `H0816 a.sham`: None who take refuge in God will be condemned/guilty, contrasting the fate of those condemned in v.21; taking refuge in God is the inner disposition that keeps one from being counted guilty. — keywords: `refuge taking`, `guilt averted`, `trust disposition`, `condemnation reversed`, `shelter divine`
- **vc=18839** Hos 5:15 `H0816 a.sham`: Guilt is here the inner state that estranges Israel from God — God withdraws until they acknowledge it — showing that recognizing and confessing guilt is the necessary first movement of conscience that opens the way back to God. — keywords: `guilt acknowledging`, `conscience awakening`, `estrangement divine`, `seeking genuine`, `guilt confession`, `return initiated`

#### M10-D-VCG-02 (19 verses)

- **vc=18903** Lev 4:3 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guilt here is not self-contained — the priest's sin propagates outward, bringing guilt upon the whole people, showing that a leader's inner moral failure has communal consequences beyond the individual. — keywords: `guilt propagating`, `communal consequence`, `leadership failure`, `sin spreading`, `moral contagion`
- **vc=18904** Lev 6:5 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness is tied to the moment of inner realization — the day one becomes consciously aware of the wrong done by false oath — which then demands full restitution plus a fifth, linking guilt to conscience and remedial action. — keywords: `guilt realization`, `conscience moment`, `restitution triggered`, `false oath`, `awareness remedial`
- **vc=18905** Lev 6:7 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness here is the state produced by any action that makes a person liable before God; priestly atonement is the remedy that removes this state and restores forgiveness. — keywords: `guilt state`, `atonement removing`, `liability produced`, `forgiveness restoring`, `priestly mediation`
- **vc=18906** Lev 22:16 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness is the state that outsiders cause the priests to bear by eating holy things unlawfully, showing guilt as a burden that can be wrongfully imposed on others through improper handling of what is sacred. — keywords: `guilt imposed`, `burden transferred`, `holiness violated`, `iniquity borne`, `priestly liability`
- **vc=18907** 1Ch 21:3 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness here is a communal moral liability—Joab warns that the king's census command would make Israel culpable before God; guilt is understood as incurred through a leader's will acting wrongly on behalf of the people. — keywords: `guilt communal`, `liability corporate`, `will warning`, `leader culpability`, `conscience cautioning`, `guilt incurred`
- **vc=18908** 2Ch 24:18 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness here is the direct cause of divine wrath—Judah's abandonment of God's house and service of idols produced a guilt that drew God's anger upon them, showing guilt as the accumulated moral liability of corporate apostasy. — keywords: `apostasy corporate`, `guilt accumulated`, `wrath triggered`, `defection covenant`, `guilt causal`, `abandonment inner`
- **vc=18909** 2Ch 28:10 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness here is a confrontational rebuke—the prophet challenges Israel's intent to enslave Judah by pointing to their own existing guilt before God, showing guilt as a personal moral debt that disqualifies one from compounding another's. — keywords: `guilt existing`, `conscience confronted`, `debt unresolved`, `rebuke moral`, `self-awareness lacking`, `guilt disqualifying`
- **vc=18910** 2Ch 28:13 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guilt here is already great and accumulating—bringing captives in would add more guilt against the Lord on top of existing sins; guilt is portrayed as a growing moral weight with a threshold that intensifies divine wrath. — keywords: `guilt accumulating`, `threshold exceeded`, `wrath intensifying`, `guilt compounding`, `moral weight growing`, `conscience warning`
- **vc=18911** 2Ch 33:23 `H0819 ash.mah`: Amon's guiltiness is portrayed as an accumulating inner state — he refused to humble himself as his father had, and instead piled up guilt progressively, showing the will actively moving away from repentance. — keywords: `guilt accumulating`, `humility refused`, `will defiant`, `repentance rejected`, `guilt progressive`, `hardening repeated`
- **vc=18902** Ezr 9:6 `H0819 ash.mah` ★: Guilt is pictured as an overwhelming inner weight — it has risen above the head and mounted to the heavens, producing shame and an inability to lift one's face before God, locating guilt in the conscience and affecting posture before him. — keywords: `shame overwhelming`, `guilt towering`, `conscience crushed`, `posture broken`, `face averted`, `guilt weight`
- **vc=18912** Ezr 9:7 `H0819 ash.mah`: Guiltiness is portrayed as a persistent generational state — 'great guilt' stretching from the fathers to the present day — that has produced concrete consequences: captivity, sword, plundering, and utter shame. — keywords: `guilt generational`, `shame persistent`, `consequence historical`, `guilt inherited`, `conscience communal`, `captivity deserved`
- **vc=18913** Ezr 9:13 `H0819 ash.mah`: Great guilt is acknowledged as the deserving cause of all the suffering that has come, yet God's judgment was less than it deserved — guiltiness here is evaluated against divine justice, revealing a conscience aware of moral debt. — keywords: `guilt deserving`, `conscience calibrated`, `mercy undeserved`, `debt moral`, `judgment measured`, `awareness divine`

### M10-E

- **vc=19479** Lev 5:1 `H5771G a.von`: Iniquity here is the moral burden the silent witness must 'bear' personally; it is the consequence that settles on the person as a result of the failure to speak, showing iniquity as a weight carried within the individual. — keywords: `silence willful`, `guilt bearing`, `omission`, `iniquity personal`, `witness suppressed`, `conscience burdened`
- **vc=19480** Lev 5:17 `H5771G a.von`: Iniquity here is the burden the individual must 'bear' as a consequence of unwitting sin; it is a weight that falls on the person once guilt is realized, showing iniquity as a personal moral load carried before God. — keywords: `transgression unwitting`, `guilt surfacing`, `iniquity bearing`, `realization guilt`, `burden personal`, `ignorance`
- **vc=19481** Lev 7:18 `H5771G a.von`: Iniquity is a moral burden the offender personally bears when he desecrates the peace offering by eating it on the third day; the wrong act transfers guilt directly onto the person, nullifying any benefit of the offering. — keywords: `desecration ritual`, `guilt transferred`, `iniquity bearing`, `offering nullified`, `profanation`, `culpability personal`
- **vc=19482** Lev 10:17 `H5771G a.von`: Iniquity here is the moral-cultic burden of the congregation that the priests are appointed to bear on their behalf through eating the sin offering, showing iniquity as a transferable load requiring priestly mediation. — keywords: `burden transferred`, `iniquity vicarious`, `mediation priestly`, `guilt communal`, `atonement bearing`, `substitution`

- **vc=35588** Hos 14:9 `H6586 pa.sha`: Transgressors here are those who stumble in the Lord's right ways, contrasted with the upright who walk in them — their inner disposition is one of resistance to God's order, causing them to trip on the very path that sustains others. — keywords: `stumbling moral`, `resistance habitual`, `wisdom lacking`, `will opposing`, `path refused`, `conscience hardened`
- **vc=35589** Amo 4:4 `H6586 pa.sha`: Transgressing here is ironically commanded at the very religious sites Israel frequents — 'come to Bethel and transgress' — exposing that their worship is itself rebellion, showing transgression as an inner defiance disguised as devotion. — keywords: `devotion false`, `defiance disguised`, `worship corrupted`, `rebellion habitual`, `conscience deceived`, `transgression multiplied`
- **vc=35590** Zep 3:11 `H6586 pa.sha`: Transgression is expressed through deeds of proud rebellion against God; on the day of restoration those deeds will no longer bring shame because the proudly exultant—the source of that rebellion—will be removed. — keywords: `pride rebellion`, `defection willful`, `haughtiness`, `shame removed`, `heart purged`
- **vc=40854** 2Jo 9 `G3845 parabainō`: To transgress here is to go ahead and leave behind the teaching of Christ — a movement of the will away from abiding that results in losing relationship with both the Father and the Son. — keywords: `will departing`, `abiding abandoned`, `relationship severed`, `truth left`, `defection progressive`

- **vc=40858** Gal 3:19 `G3847 parabasis`: The law was added to address transgressions — human violations of divine commands — and was meant to serve this purpose only until the promised offspring came, giving transgression a historically bounded function. — keywords: `transgression named`, `law constraining`, `violation defined`, `conscience bounded`, `transgression historical`
- **vc=40859** 1Ti 2:14 `G3847 parabasis`: Eve's transgression resulted from being deceived — the inner faculty of perception was corrupted through deception, leading to a crossing of God's command, while Adam sinned without that deception. — keywords: `deception corrupting`, `perception subverted`, `will led astray`, `transgression deceived`, `conscience overridden`

- **vc=40861** Heb 9:15 `G3847 parabasis`: Transgressions committed under the first covenant are the liability from which Christ's death redeems — they are legal-moral offenses that bound the guilty to condemnation until the new covenant's atoning death released them. — keywords: `guilt covenantal`, `liability atoned`, `condemnation released`, `transgression redeemed`, `atonement liberating`

- **vc=40874** Rom 5:18 `G3900 paraptōma`: One trespass led to universal condemnation for all men, directly mirrored by one act of righteousness leading to justification for all; the trespass is the moral pivot point that determined the condemned status of the entire human race. — keywords: `trespass universal`, `condemnation inherited`, `moral pivot`, `status determined`, `guilt transmitted`

- **vc=21711** Pro 12:8 `H5753A a.vah`: A twisted mind results in social contempt; the inner faculty of thought or understanding is morally warped, and this distortion of the mind is what earns the person despise. — keywords: `mind warped`, `moral distortion`, `understanding twisted`, `contempt earned`, `character corrupt`
- **vc=21714** Isa 21:3 `H5753A a.vah`: The term here describes being physically bowed down by anguish — the prophet's body is bent/twisted by the overwhelming inner pain of the vision, showing the twisting as an effect of extreme anguish on the person's constitution. — keywords: `anguish overwhelming`, `body twisted`, `vision distress`, `constitution bent`, `perception impaired`, `suffering visceral`
- **vc=32859** Isa 29:16 `H2017 ho.phekh` ★: Perversity here is a cognitive-relational inversion — the creature's mind is so twisted it denies the creator made it and denies his understanding, reversing the proper order of creature-dependence and creator-authority. — keywords: `inversion cognitive`, `creator denied`, `creature defiant`, `authority rejected`, `mind reversed`, `dependence refused`
- **vc=21715** Jer 3:21 `H5753A a.vah`: Perverting their way is linked directly to forgetting God; the inner twisting of the will and direction of life leads to spiritual amnesia—the weeping heard shows the resulting distress once the perversion's consequences are felt. — keywords: `way perverted`, `god forgotten`, `will twisted`, `amnesia spiritual`, `distress consequential`, `direction lost`
- **vc=19471** Jer 9:5 `H5753B a.vah`: Perverting iniquity is described as a habitual practice that people deliberately teach their tongues; it is a willed, cultivated inner corruption—they weary themselves committing it—showing perversity as chosen and ingrained. — keywords: `tongue trained`, `lying habitual`, `iniquity cultivated`, `perversity willed`, `corruption ingrained`, `deception practiced`
- **vc=21716** Lam 3:9 `H5753A a.vah`: God is described as making the sufferer's paths crooked; the verse uses twisting/perverting to portray divine action blocking the person's way, depicting the inner experience of disorientation and blocked progress under judgment. — keywords: `path blocked`, `way crooked`, `disorientation inner`, `judgment experienced`, `progress denied`, `divine constraint`
- **vc=24220** Eze 9:9 `H4297 mut.teh`: Perversion fills the city as injustice: twisted structures of social order reflecting an inner moral distortion so complete that the people have convinced themselves God neither sees nor cares. — keywords: `injustice pervasive`, `conscience suppressed`, `divine oversight denied`, `moral distortion systemic`, `self-deception`, `guilt collective`
- **vc=19472** Dan 9:5 `H5753B a.vah`: To pervert here means to twist or distort righteous conduct; placed between sinning and acting wickedly, it names the inner bending of moral direction away from God's rules as part of total moral failure. — keywords: `moral direction bent`, `rebellion layered`, `conscience confessing`, `commandment abandoned`, `wrong compounded`, `contrition total`

#### M10-H-VCG-04 (4 verses)

- **vc=7222** 1Ti 6:5 `G1311 diaftheirō`: The mind is the specific faculty that is depraved — corruption has penetrated to the seat of understanding, so that the person is robbed of truth and distorts even godliness into a scheme for personal gain. — keywords: `mind depraved`, `truth lost`, `understanding corrupted`, `motive distorted`, `godliness twisted`, `cognition ruined`

### M10-I

#### M10-I-VCG-01 (20 verses)

- **vc=21723** Lev 19:15 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice in the courtroom is warned against as a failure of right judgment — partiality toward either poor or powerful corrupts the judicial process; the opposite of injustice here is impartial righteousness in judging one's neighbor. — keywords: `judgment partial`, `partiality`, `will corrupted`, `fairness violated`, `conscience failing`, `righteousness absent`
- **vc=21724** Lev 19:35 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is prohibited in commercial and legal measurement — falsifying weights or quantities is named as moral wrong, showing injustice as an act of the will that violates fairness and integrity in everyday dealings. — keywords: `will deceiving`, `integrity violated`, `fairness corrupted`, `dishonesty commercial`, `moral violation`
- **vc=21725** Deu 25:16 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice here is dishonest commercial behavior—acting with fraudulent measures; those who act this way are called an abomination to God, showing that unjust dealing in the marketplace corrupts one's standing before him. — keywords: `dishonesty habitual`, `will fraudulent`, `abomination`, `standing corrupted`, `defection commercial`
- **vc=65852** Deu 32:4 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is here used negatively to define God's character: he is entirely without it, being just and upright by nature; the term's absence in God marks the standard against which all human injustice is measured. — keywords: `divine purity`, `standard absolute`, `injustice absent`, `character perfect`, `uprightness divine`
- **vc=21721** Job 34:10 `H5766A a.vel`: Elihu affirms it is unthinkable that God would commit injustice or wrong, establishing God's inner moral character as structurally opposed to the doing of any injustice. — keywords: `divine character`, `injustice impossible`, `moral opposition`, `will holy`, `wrongdoing unthinkable`
- **vc=21726** Job 34:32 `H5766A a.vel`: The penitent asks to be taught unseen wrongs and pledges to stop doing injustice once it is identified, showing injustice as a moral failing one must be enlightened to recognize and then willfully abandon. — keywords: `blindness moral`, `enlightenment sought`, `will abandoning`, `repentance conditional`, `injustice unseen`, `awareness lacking`
- **vc=21727** Psa 7:3 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is located in the hands as the instrument of wrongdoing; the psalmist protests innocence by declaring there is no such wrong in his hands, grounding moral accountability in deeds. — keywords: `innocence claimed`, `accountability moral`, `conscience protesting`, `deeds examined`, `self-vindication`
- **vc=21728** Psa 53:1 `H5766A a.vel` ★: Injustice here flows from the inner denial of God; the fool's heart-assertion that God does not exist produces corrupt, abominable conduct, showing that inward godlessness drives outward wrongdoing. — keywords: `heart denial`, `godlessness inner`, `corruption spreading`, `will defecting`, `conscience suppressed`
- **vc=21729** Psa 82:2 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice here is a pattern of corrupt judicial action — judging unjustly and favoring the wicked — showing it as an ongoing inner disposition corrupting the exercise of authority. — keywords: `partiality habitual`, `authority corrupted`, `will biased`, `judgment perverted`, `disposition ongoing`
- **vc=21730** Pro 29:27 `H5766A a.vel`: The unjust man embodies a moral character so antithetical to righteousness that he is an abomination to the righteous — injustice and integrity are shown as fundamentally opposite inner orientations. — keywords: `orientation moral`, `character antithetical`, `revulsion mutual`, `identity unjust`, `abomination felt`
- **vc=21731** Jer 2:5 `H5766A a.vel`: God charges that his people found no injustice or wrong in him, yet still chose to depart; the inner movement away from God is therefore groundless, driven not by any fault in God but by the will's pull toward worthless idols. — keywords: `will departing`, `groundless defection`, `idolatry pull`, `god abandoned`, `worthlessness pursuing`
- **vc=21722** Eze 3:20 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is what a formerly righteous person commits when they turn from righteousness; it is the active moral perversion—opposite of righteousness—that, once committed, brings a divine stumbling block and death. — keywords: `turning apostasy`, `righteousness abandoned`, `will reversing`, `threshold crossed`, `death consequential`
- **vc=21732** Eze 18:8 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is something the righteous man actively withholds his hand from—a refusal to act unjustly—suggesting injustice is understood as a potential act of the will that must be consciously restrained. — keywords: `will restraining`, `hand withheld`, `injustice resisted`, `conscious refusal`, `self-control moral`
- **vc=21733** Eze 18:24 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is the first act the righteous person does upon turning away from righteousness—it is the initial breach, followed by abominations, indicating that injustice marks the threshold crossing from righteousness to wickedness. — keywords: `threshold crossing`, `righteousness forfeited`, `will defecting`, `breach initial`, `apostasy progressive`
- **vc=21734** Eze 18:26 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is the act for which the formerly righteous person dies; the verse repeats the point for emphasis—injustice done after righteousness is its own lethal offense, fully owned by the one who commits it. — keywords: `ownership moral`, `death deserved`, `injustice owned`, `will accountable`, `reversal lethal`
- **vc=21735** Eze 28:15 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is portrayed as something that emerged from within a previously blameless being; it was not original to the cherub but was 'found' in him, marking a moral rupture from within. — keywords: `corruption emerging`, `blamelessness lost`, `rupture inner`, `unrighteousness surfacing`, `origin internal`
- **vc=21736** Eze 28:18 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice in trade profaned the cherub's own sanctuaries; it is depicted as a commercial-moral corruption operating from within, drawing divine fire out from the very midst of the offender. — keywords: `corruption commercial`, `sanctity profaned`, `inward disorder`, `judgment consuming`, `guilt compounding`
- **vc=21737** Eze 33:13 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice done by the righteous who trusts his own righteousness erases all his prior good deeds; the verse locates the fatal danger in an act of injustice arising from misplaced self-confidence. — keywords: `self-trust misplaced`, `confidence false`, `injustice fatal`, `merit erased`, `will presumptuous`
- **vc=21738** Eze 33:15 `H5766A a.vel`: Injustice is defined here by its opposite: the wicked who stops practicing it—by restoring pledges and walking in righteous statutes—shall live; abstaining from injustice is the path to life. — keywords: `abstaining deliberate`, `will turning`, `restitution restoring`, `injustice ceased`, `life renewed`
- **vc=21739** Eze 33:18 `H5766A a.vel`: When a righteous person turns to injustice, the act itself becomes lethal; the verse makes clear that injustice is not a minor lapse but a fatal turning of the will that forfeits life. — keywords: `will turning`, `defection wilful`, `righteousness forfeited`, `death consequence`, `direction reversal`

- **vc=21744** 1Ch 17:9 `H5766B av.lah`: Injustice here appears only by its structural opposite: God's promise of a secure place where 'violent men shall waste them no more' implies injustice is the violent, destabilizing force that God's planting of Israel will end. — keywords: `violence destabilizing`, `oppression force`, `wickedness external`, `harm recurring`, `restraint divine`

- **vc=21761** Psa 107:42 `H5766B av.lah`: Wickedness (injustice) is silenced when God's righteous acts are displayed; it is personified as a voice that shuts its mouth before divine justice, showing it as fundamentally unable to stand before God's order. — keywords: `wickedness silenced`, `voice suppressed`, `shame enforced`, `justice confronting`, `defiance collapsed`
- **vc=21762** Psa 119:3 `H5766B av.lah`: Doing no wrong is the behavioral mark of those who walk in God's ways; injustice is defined by its absence — it is what the obedient heart and life do not do, making it the structural opposite of covenant faithfulness. — keywords: `obedience inner`, `wrongdoing absent`, `covenant faithfulness`, `will aligned`, `wrong avoided`
- **vc=21763** Psa 125:3 `H5766B av.lah`: Injustice is a contagious pressure; prolonged exposure to its rule over the land could tempt even the righteous into doing wrong, showing it as an external force capable of corrupting the inner will. — keywords: `contagion moral`, `will pressured`, `corruption external`, `righteous tempted`, `resistance eroding`
- **vc=21764** Pro 22:8 `H5766B av.lah`: Injustice is the seed sown that produces calamity; the verse frames moral wrongdoing as an active, deliberate planting whose consequences are inescapable and proportional. — keywords: `sowing deliberate`, `consequence inevitable`, `wrongdoing planted`, `retribution proportional`, `will reaping`
- **vc=21765** Isa 59:3 `H5766B av.lah`: Injustice/wickedness is expressed through the tongue that mutters it — it flows outward through speech as a persistent inner moral disorder made audible in words. — keywords: `speech corrupt`, `tongue expressing`, `disorder moral`, `wickedness audible`, `inward overflow`
- **vc=21766** Isa 61:8 `H5766B av.lah`: Injustice/wrong is something God hates as the structural opposite of the justice he loves — here it appears as robbery and wrong paired together, standing against God's commitment to faithful recompense and covenant. — keywords: `divine hatred`, `aversion moral`, `justice loved`, `wrong rejected`, `covenant contrasted`
- **vc=21767** Hos 10:13 `H5766B av.lah`: Injustice here is the bitter harvest of a morally corrupted will — they plowed iniquity and reaped injustice — showing it as the inevitable fruit of inner choices, compounded by self-trust rather than reliance on God. — keywords: `self trust`, `harvest moral`, `will corrupted`, `iniquity cultivated`, `reliance misplaced`, `fruit bitter`

- **vc=18943** Job 7:20 `H2398 cha.ta`: Job asks what harm his sin could possibly do to God, the watcher of mankind — showing sin here as a moral act directed against God that raises a question about its effects on the divine-human relationship and Job's burden of being divinely observed. — keywords: `surveillance divine`, `burden felt`, `sin relational`, `questioning inner`, `exposure moral`

- **vc=18960** Jer 3:25 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning against God is confessed as spanning from youth to the present day, a lifelong pattern covering both the current generation and their fathers; it produces shame that covers them, placing sin at the root of their dishonor. — keywords: `shame covering`, `confession corporate`, `sin generational`, `dishonor felt`, `pattern lifelong`
- **vc=18958** Jer 14:7 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning against God is confessed amid a plea for God to act for his own name's sake; sin is acknowledged as having produced the desperate state, yet the appeal is that God's glory transcends the people's sinful record. — keywords: `confession plea`, `backsliding repeated`, `sin acknowledged`, `appeal divine`, `guilt admitted`
- **vc=18957** Jer 14:20 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning against God is openly acknowledged alongside the inherited iniquity of the fathers; the corporate confession shows sin as a recognized inner reality that encompasses generations and stands in need of divine action. — keywords: `wickedness acknowledged`, `iniquity inherited`, `confession corporate`, `sin recognized`, `generational guilt`
- **vc=18969** Lam 5:7 `H2398 cha.ta`: Fathers sinned and are gone, but the present generation bears their iniquities; sin is shown as an act by one generation whose moral consequences are inherited and carried by those who follow, even the innocent. — keywords: `iniquity inherited`, `consequence transferred`, `guilt generational`, `burden carried`, `sin transmitted`
- **vc=19046** Eze 33:16 `H2398 cha.ta`: Past sins committed by the repentant wicked person are no longer held in divine memory; the verse shows that committed sins can be fully cancelled when the person turns to justice and right. — keywords: `sin cancelled`, `memory divine`, `repentance transforming`, `guilt erased`, `record cleared`, `turning redemptive`

#### M10-L-VCG-03 (1 verses)

- **vc=18980** Deu 1:41 `H2398 cha.ta` ★: The people confess sin against the Lord but immediately proceed to act on their own initiative; this exposes a pattern where verbal acknowledgment of sin does not produce genuine inner repentance, as the will moves forward independently of God's direction. — keywords: `confession hollow`, `repentance absent`, `will autonomous`, `acknowledgment verbal`, `self-initiative`, `obedience bypassed`

### M10-M

- **vc=18959** Jer 2:35 `H2398 cha.ta` ★: Sinning is compounded by the inner denial of having sinned; the person claims innocence and assumes God's anger has passed, but God declares he will judge precisely for this self-deception about one's own sinful state. — keywords: `self-deception`, `innocence claimed`, `conscience suppressed`, `denial sinful`, `judgment compounded`
- **vc=19020** Jer 16:10 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning against God is something the people fail to recognize despite facing severe judgment; their question—'what sin have we committed?'—reveals a conscience that has lost awareness of its own sinful inner state. — keywords: `conscience blinded`, `awareness absent`, `sin unrecognized`, `self-ignorance`, `judgment uncomprehended`
- **vc=37520** 1Cor 15:34 `G0264 hamartanō`: Ongoing sinning is linked to a state of ignorance about God — continuing in sin reflects a failure of right knowledge and spiritual alertness, and Paul names it to provoke shame and awakening. — keywords: `ignorance persisting`, `alertness lacking`, `sin ongoing`, `shame invoked`, `awakening urged`
- **vc=37554** Tit 3:11 `G0264 hamartanō`: The divisive person is described as warped and sinful, self-condemned — sin here reflects an entrenched inner distortion of character that the person's own conscience implicitly witnesses against. — keywords: `conscience self-condemning`, `character warped`, `self-condemnation`, `distortion entrenched`, `sin habitual`

- **vc=19044** Eze 18:24 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sin committed by the formerly righteous person—having turned from righteousness—is the specific offense for which he dies; it is a conscious act of treachery that eclipses all prior righteous deeds. — keywords: `righteousness forfeited`, `turning defection`, `treachery conscious`, `prior merit erased`, `will reversing`, `sin fatal`

- **vc=37608** Mat 26:65 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The high priest declares Jesus' claim blasphemy — a verbal act he treats as a capital offense against God — using it to close the trial and secure a death sentence. — keywords: `claim divine`, `authority usurped`, `speech condemned`, `blasphemy declared`, `verdict closed`
- **vc=37609** Mar 2:7 `G0988 blasfēmia` ★: The scribes charge Jesus with blasphemy because he claims to forgive sins, treating this as a usurpation of divine authority — the inner offense is presumptuous speech that trespasses on God's exclusive role. — keywords: `authority divine`, `prerogative usurped`, `presumption perceived`, `boundary transgressed`, `forgiveness claimed`
- **vc=37610** Mar 3:28 `G0988 blasfēmia`: Whatever blasphemies people utter are included in the category of forgivable offenses, setting up the contrast with the single unforgivable blasphemy against the Holy Spirit in the next verse. — keywords: `forgiveness available`, `guilt forgivable`, `speech offensive`, `blasphemy categorized`, `mercy framed`
- **vc=37611** Mar 14:64 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The council declares Jesus' speech blasphemy and unanimously condemns him to death, treating the word as a capital offense — the inner act of arrogating divine status is judged fatal. — keywords: `claim divine`, `authority arrogated`, `condemnation unanimous`, `blasphemy capital`, `verdict fatal`
- **vc=37612** Luk 5:21 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The scribes and Pharisees hear Jesus' forgiveness declaration as blasphemy — a usurpation of God's exclusive prerogative — showing that the inner offense of blasphemy is defined here as improper claim to divine authority. — keywords: `authority divine`, `prerogative claimed`, `presumption charged`, `forgiveness exclusive`, `blasphemy perceived`
- **vc=37613** Joh 10:33 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The Jews charge Jesus with blasphemy specifically because he, a man, claims to be God—blasphemy here is the inner presumption of claiming divine identity, treated as an offense deserving death. — keywords: `presumption divine`, `identity claimed`, `blasphemy charged`, `transgression perceived`, `honor sacred`

#### M10-R-VCG-03 (6 verses)

- **vc=37627** 2Pe 2:11 `G0989 blasfēmos`: Even mighty angels restrain themselves from uttering a blasphemous verdict against spiritual beings before God, showing that such speech exceeds what any creature's will should presume to exercise. — keywords: `will restrained`, `presumption withheld`, `speech deferred`, `authority creaturely`, `restraint willful`
- **vc=37623** Rev 2:9 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The blasphemy here is a false verbal claim — those who call themselves Jews but are not slander the true community, so blasphemy operates as a lying assertion that defames what is genuinely God's. — keywords: `identity false`, `assertion lying`, `defamation verbal`, `claim fabricated`, `slander identity`, `truth assaulted`
- **vc=37615** Rev 13:1 `G0988 blasfēmia` ★: The beast bears blasphemous names inscribed on its very heads — blasphemy is not an act here but a constitutive identity marker, the creature's nature defined by its arrogant claim against God. — keywords: `identity constitutive`, `defiance inscribed`, `nature blasphemous`, `arrogance essential`, `character total`, `being marked`
- **vc=37616** Rev 13:5 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The beast's mouth, given to uttering haughty and blasphemous words, exercises a permitted authority — blasphemy functions here as an empowered, willful, prolonged assault on God through speech. — keywords: `will empowered`, `speech defiant`, `assault prolonged`, `authority permitted`, `haughtiness vocal`, `defiance wilful`
- **vc=37607** Rev 13:6 `G0988 blasfēmia`: Blasphemy is directed at God's name, his heavenly dwelling, and those who dwell there — it is a comprehensive verbal assault from the will, targeting God's identity, his presence, and his people. — keywords: `assault comprehensive`, `name targeted`, `will aggressive`, `presence targeted`, `defiance verbal`, `speech assaulting`
- **vc=37617** Rev 17:3 `G0988 blasfēmia`: The beast is covered in blasphemous names as its defining characteristic — blasphemy saturates its very being, making defiance of God not an occasional act but the creature's total nature. — keywords: `defiance total`, `nature saturated`, `identity blasphemous`, `being constituted`, `character comprehensive`, `defection ontological`

### M10-T

- **vc=19715** Mat 9:6 `G0266 hamartia`: Sins are what the Son of Man has authority to forgive on earth—this authority is explicitly demonstrated through physical healing, showing sin as a condition requiring divine jurisdiction to remove. — keywords: `forgiveness divine`, `authority releasing`, `guilt removed`, `sin condition`, `healing linked`
- **vc=19710** Mat 12:31 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin here is presented as something forgivable when committed against people or in general, establishing it as an offense that divine mercy can cover, unlike the uniquely unforgivable blasphemy against the Spirit. — keywords: `forgiveness scope`, `blasphemy unforgivable`, `mercy covering`, `sin forgivable`, `limit divine`

- **vc=19730** Rom 5:13 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin existed as a reality in the world even before the law gave it formal definition; it is not legally counted without law, yet its presence and lethal effect are real, showing sin is an ontological condition prior to any explicit moral code. — keywords: `sin ontological`, `law absent`, `transgression uncounted`, `guilt latent`, `condemnation deferred`
