- **vc=19732** Rom 5:21 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is described as having 'reigned in death,' portraying it as a tyrannical ruling power whose dominion over the person leads to death; grace's counter-reign through righteousness shows sin's reign is a competing authority within human existence. — keywords: `sin reigning`, `dominion tyrannical`, `death ruling`, `allegiance transferred`, `counter-reign grace`
- **vc=19744** Rom 6:6 `G0266 hamartia`: The 'body of sin' is the old self's bodily existence oriented toward sin as master; crucifying the old self aims at destroying sin's bodily dominion so that the person is no longer enslaved to it, showing sin as a master that colonizes the body. — keywords: `enslavement bodily`, `old self crucified`, `body colonized`, `dominion destroyed`, `liberation embodied`
- **vc=19745** Rom 6:7 `G0266 hamartia`: Death itself is presented as the mechanism of liberation from sin's power, showing sin as a master or enslavement from which one can only be freed by dying; it holds the living person in bondage that only dissolution of the old self can break. — keywords: `death liberating`, `bondage severed`, `enslavement ended`, `self dissolved`, `freedom death`
- **vc=19733** Rom 6:10 `G0266 hamartia`: Christ died to sin 'once for all,' meaning his death was a definitive termination of any relationship to sin's domain; sin is the sphere of mortal existence he exited permanently, establishing the pattern for the believer's own death to it. — keywords: `death definitive`, `domain exited`, `sin sphere`, `departure final`, `allegiance ended`
- **vc=19734** Rom 6:11 `G0266 hamartia`: Believers are to reckon themselves as dead to sin in their minds and wills, indicating that dying to sin requires a conscious act of self-assessment; sin remains a domain the believer must cognitively refuse allegiance to through ongoing mental reckoning. — keywords: `reckoning conscious`, `mind refusing`, `self assessment`, `allegiance cognitive`, `will reorienting`
- **vc=19735** Rom 6:12 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is addressed as a would-be king attempting to reign in the mortal body through its passions; it seeks to co-opt bodily desires as instruments of its rule, meaning it operates through the body's appetites to assert dominion over the whole person. — keywords: `sin reigning`, `body commandeered`, `passions enlisted`, `dominion resisted`, `appetite subverted`
- **vc=19736** Rom 6:13 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is the recipient to whom one may wrongly present bodily members as instruments of unrighteousness; this frames sin as a commander who deploys the body's capacities for destructive ends, and the will's decision determines whose instruments the members become. — keywords: `members surrendered`, `will deciding`, `body instrument`, `allegiance offered`, `self presenting`
- **vc=19724** Rom 6:14 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is denied dominion over the believer because they are under grace rather than law; sin's power to dominate is tied to the law's role in generating condemnation, so grace removes the legal ground on which sin's tyranny over the person stood. — keywords: `dominion denied`, `grace liberating`, `law removed`, `sin overthrown`, `tyranny ended`
- **vc=19737** Rom 6:16 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is one of two masters a person can be enslaved to through obedience — sin leading to death, obedience to righteousness; the choice of whose slave one becomes is made at the level of the will, as the inner decision of whom to obey determines the master. — keywords: `will enslaved`, `obedience choosing`, `master chosen`, `allegiance surrendered`, `death trajectory`
- **vc=19738** Rom 6:17 `G0266 hamartia`: Former slavery to sin is contrasted with present heart-obedience to sound doctrine; sin's former mastery was over the whole person, but conversion involved a decisive inner turn — from the heart — that transferred allegiance away from sin's authority. — keywords: `heart transferred`, `slavery former`, `obedience heart`, `allegiance converted`, `inner turning`
- **vc=19739** Rom 6:18 `G0266 hamartia`: Being freed from sin and enslaved to righteousness are presented as mutually exclusive states; liberation from sin is not mere moral improvement but a change of master, relocating the person's inner allegiance from sin's dominion to righteousness entirely. — keywords: `liberation total`, `master transferred`, `allegiance relocated`, `enslavement ended`, `righteousness owned`
- **vc=19741** Rom 6:20 `G0266 hamartia`: When enslaved to sin, one was entirely free from righteousness — sin and righteousness are mutually exclusive masters; this shows sin's enslavement was total, leaving no inner space for righteousness, constituting the whole person as sin's possession. — keywords: `enslavement total`, `righteousness excluded`, `inner space absent`, `possession complete`, `allegiance singular`
- **vc=19742** Rom 6:22 `G0266 hamartia`: Freedom from sin produces fruit leading to sanctification and eternal life; sin's former mastery was a condition that blocked this growth entirely, showing that liberation from sin is the precondition for any progress toward holiness and ultimate life with God. — keywords: `liberation fruitful`, `sanctification growing`, `sin blocking`, `holiness preconditioned`, `freedom productive`
- **vc=19743** Rom 6:23 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin pays wages — death — in stark contrast to God's free gift of eternal life; sin is here an employer whose entire compensation to the person it uses is death, making service to it a self-destructive inner allegiance with a fatal and certain outcome. — keywords: `death wages`, `sin employing`, `self destructive`, `allegiance fatal`, `outcome certain`
- **vc=19752** Rom 7:5 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is portrayed as passions operating within the body's members, aroused by the law while a person lives according to the flesh, producing fruit that leads to death. — keywords: `passions aroused`, `flesh operating`, `law provoking`, `members activated`, `desire lethal`
- **vc=19725** Rom 7:7 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is that which the law makes knowable to the mind and conscience; without the commandment 'do not covet,' the inner reality of covetous desire as sin would have remained unrecognized. — keywords: `sin named`, `conscience awakened`, `desire recognized`, `law revealing`, `covetousness identified`
- **vc=19753** Rom 7:8 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is personified as an inner force that seizes the commandment as an opportunity to produce all kinds of covetous desire within the person; apart from law, it lies dormant. — keywords: `sin opportunistic`, `desire produced`, `law exploited`, `covetousness aroused`, `dormancy broken`
- **vc=19754** Rom 7:9 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is portrayed as a dormant power that springs to life within the person when the commandment arrives, with the result that the person experiences a kind of spiritual death. — keywords: `sin awakened`, `dormancy ended`, `law arriving`, `spiritual death`, `power activated`
- **vc=19746** Rom 7:11 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin, using the commandment as its instrument, operates deceptively within the person, exploiting what is good to kill — revealing sin's fundamentally deceptive and lethal inner power. — keywords: `deception inner`, `sin deceiving`, `commandment exploited`, `death produced`, `will subverted`
- **vc=19747** Rom 7:13 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin works death in the person through what is good, thereby exposing its own true character — it is shown to be utterly sinful, exploiting the good commandment to produce death beyond measure. — keywords: `sin exposed`, `good exploited`, `death produced`, `sin revealed`, `conscience illumined`
- **vc=19748** Rom 7:14 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin functions as a master to which the flesh-bound person is sold, depicting a state of inner enslavement where the self is under sin's ownership and control. — keywords: `enslavement total`, `flesh owned`, `self sold`, `will captive`, `inner bondage`
- **vc=19721** Rom 7:17 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is depicted as a power that takes up residence within the person, such that actions the person does not will are attributed to this indwelling force rather than to the self's own agency. — keywords: `agency hijacked`, `indwelling power`, `will displaced`, `self disowned`, `sin residing`
- **vc=19749** Rom 7:20 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is located as an indwelling force within the self, distinct from the person's conscious will—it operates inside the person, overriding chosen intent, revealing it as a constitutional inner power that hijacks agency from within. — keywords: `agency hijacked`, `will overridden`, `indwelling power`, `self disowned`, `intent subverted`
- **vc=19750** Rom 7:23 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin functions as a competing law lodged in the body's members, waging war against the mind's law and taking the person captive — depicting an internal conflict between mind and flesh. — keywords: `inner conflict`, `mind warring`, `captivity inner`, `law competing`, `will opposed`, `flesh resisting`
- **vc=19751** Rom 7:25 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin operates through the flesh as a governing law, standing in sharp contrast to the law of God served by the mind — revealing a divided inner person where mind and flesh serve opposing masters. — keywords: `self divided`, `mind serving`, `flesh serving`, `allegiance split`, `inner duality`, `will bifurcated`
- **vc=19726** Rom 8:2 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is presented as a law paired with death that once held the person captive, from which the Spirit's law in Christ Jesus has now brought liberation. — keywords: `captivity released`, `liberation inner`, `bondage broken`, `sin law`, `freedom granted`
- **vc=19727** Rom 8:3 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is the power dwelling in sinful flesh that God condemns through Christ's incarnation, depicting sin as something embedded in fleshly human nature that required divine action to defeat. — keywords: `flesh corrupted`, `sin embodied`, `condemnation divine`, `nature sinful`, `defeat sin`
- **vc=19755** Rom 8:10 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is the cause of the body's death — the physical body bears the consequence of sin — while the indwelling Spirit brings life through righteousness as the contrasting inner reality. — keywords: `body dying`, `sin consequence`, `spirit alive`, `righteousness contrasted`, `death bearing`
- **vc=19775** Rom 14:23 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is defined here as action not proceeding from faith — it is rooted in the inner disposition of doubt, making the conscience and its alignment with faith the determining factor of whether an act is sinful. — keywords: `doubt sinning`, `conscience violated`, `faith absent`, `inner misalignment`, `conviction overridden`, `act faithless`
- **vc=37522** 1Cor 7:28 `G0264 hamartanō`: Marriage is explicitly declared not a sin — the verse uses the term negatively to clarify that neither marrying nor a betrothed woman marrying constitutes a moral transgression. — keywords: `conscience cleared`, `transgression absent`, `judgment corrected`, `freedom affirmed`, `anxiety removed`
- **vc=37523** 1Cor 7:36 `G0264 hamartanō`: Marriage in response to strong passions is explicitly declared not a sin — the verse uses the negative to free the conscience of one whose inner desires make celibacy untenable. — keywords: `conscience freed`, `passion strong`, `transgression absent`, `desire acknowledged`, `will permitted`
- **vc=19728** 1Cor 15:17 `G0266 hamartia`: Sins are presented as a condition in which people remain if Christ has not been raised — without resurrection, faith is futile and the person is still held under sin, showing resurrection as the ground of sin's defeat. — keywords: `sin remaining`, `captivity unreleased`, `faith futile`, `bondage persistent`, `resurrection absent`
- **vc=19676** 2Cor 11:7 `G0266 hamartia`: Paul questions whether humbling himself by preaching free of charge constituted a sin — the verse uses the term rhetorically to challenge any perception that self-lowering for the gospel is a moral wrong. — keywords: `conscience questioning`, `humility misjudged`, `sin rhetorical`, `self lowering`, `perception wrong`
- **vc=19766** Gal 2:17 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin appears here as the charge that would fall on Jewish believers if seeking justification in Christ means they are found to be sinners like Gentiles — Paul denies this makes Christ a promoter of sin. — keywords: `sinner status`, `justification sought`, `charge deflected`, `identity threatened`, `conscience probed`
- **vc=19765** Eph 2:1 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is here a state that produces spiritual death — the person is entirely dead in it, meaning sins are not merely acts but a condition that extinguishes inner spiritual life. — keywords: `spiritual death`, `sin condition`, `life extinguished`, `inner lifeless`, `deadness total`
- **vc=19761** 1Th 2:16 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin is portrayed as accumulating to a full measure — the persecutors' inner rebellion against God has been filling up over time until divine wrath finally falls, showing sin as a progressively growing inner offense. — keywords: `sin accumulating`, `rebellion progressive`, `measure filling`, `wrath deserved`, `defection habitual`, `inner hardening`
- **vc=19762** 1Ti 5:22 `G0266 hamartia`: Hastily endorsing others can make one share in their sins — the verse warns that complicity through action implicates the inner conscience, urging self-purity by not entangling oneself in others' moral failures. — keywords: `complicity`, `conscience implicated`, `purity guarded`, `sin shared`, `entanglement moral`, `will warned`
- **vc=19763** 1Ti 5:24 `G0266 hamartia`: Sins differ in their visibility — some are evident before judgment, others surface only later, showing that sin can be concealed within the person for a time but will ultimately be revealed. — keywords: `sin concealed`, `guilt surfacing`, `visibility deferred`, `sin conspicuous`, `revelation eventual`, `judgment approaching`
- **vc=19764** 2Ti 3:6 `G0266 hamartia`: Sins burden the inner person — weak women are captured precisely because they are weighed down by accumulated sins and driven by passions, making them vulnerable to deceptive teaching. — keywords: `sin burden`, `vulnerability inner`, `passions driving`, `will weakened`, `conscience captive`, `deception received`
- **vc=19687** Heb 1:3 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin requires purification that only Christ can make — the verse presents sin as a defilement requiring an act of cleansing before the Son can take his exalted position, underscoring sin's separating power. — keywords: `defilement`, `purification needed`, `sin separating`, `access blocked`, `cleansing divine`
- **vc=19688** Heb 2:17 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin creates a standing offense between humanity and God that requires propitiation — Christ's incarnation was necessary specifically to make that atoning provision for the people's sins. — keywords: `sin offense`, `propitiation needed`, `standing ruptured`, `mediation required`, `atonement`, `guilt standing`
- **vc=19729** Heb 3:13 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin operates through deceitfulness — it works on the inner faculty of perception and the heart, hardening it gradually, making daily mutual exhortation necessary to counter its deceptive inner grip. — keywords: `heart hardening`, `sin deceptive`, `perception dulled`, `gradual corruption`, `will deceived`, `exhortation countering`
- **vc=19760** Heb 4:15 `G0266 hamartia`: Christ was tempted yet remained without sin — sin is here the boundary that was not crossed, defining it as that which a fully human person facing real temptation can nonetheless refuse, establishing its nature as a matter of the will. — keywords: `temptation real`, `will refusing`, `sin boundary`, `purity maintained`, `pressure resisted`, `sympathy earned`
- **vc=19689** Heb 5:1 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin creates the need for ongoing sacrificial mediation — the high priest's appointed role is to act between humanity and God by offering sacrifices for sins, showing sin as the persistent obstacle to divine access. — keywords: `sin persistent`, `access blocked`, `mediation required`, `sacrifice ongoing`, `separation divine`, `guilt persistent`
- **vc=19690** Heb 5:3 `G0266 hamartia`: The human high priest shares in sin himself and must offer for his own sins before the people's — sin is a shared human condition that disqualifies even the priest from standing before God without atoning sacrifice. — keywords: `shared sinfulness`, `self-implication`, `guilt personal`, `atonement self`, `human condition`, `priestly limitation`
- **vc=19691** Heb 7:27 `G0266 hamartia`: Human high priests must first sacrifice for their own sins because they share in the common sinful condition — sin inheres in the human priests themselves, requiring personal atonement before intercession for others. — keywords: `sin inherent`, `self-atonement required`, `priestly limitation`, `once-for-all`, `guilt personal`, `shared condition`

### M10-U

#### M10-U-VCG-01 (9 verses)

- **vc=19720** Joh 8:34 `G0266 hamartia` ★: Practicing sin makes one a slave to sin—Jesus describes sin as a dominating inner master that subjugates the will of the one who habitually commits it. — keywords: `will enslaved`, `bondage habitual`, `mastery sin`, `compulsion inner`, `freedom lost`
- **vc=19723** Rom 6:1 `G0266 hamartia`: The rhetorical question asks whether one should continue in sin to magnify grace; sin is here treated as a behavioral domain in which a person can persist or not, suggesting it is an ongoing pattern of life under a power one can choose to remain in. — keywords: `persistence chosen`, `domain continued`, `will rationalizing`, `grace misused`, `sin habitual`
- **vc=19740** Rom 6:2 `G0266 hamartia`: Believers are described as having died to sin, making continued living in it a contradiction; sin is a sphere of existence or a ruling domain one can be dead to, such that ongoing life in it is incompatible with the death-and-resurrection identity of the believer. — keywords: `death identity`, `domain exited`, `sin sphere`, `self contradiction`, `allegiance severed`
- **vc=19767** Gal 3:22 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin functions as a universal imprisoning power under which all of Scripture confines everything, so that the promise cannot be attained by human effort but only by faith in Christ. — keywords: `imprisonment universal`, `sin confining`, `will helpless`, `promise blocked`, `faith required`
- **vc=37525** Eph 4:26 `G0264 hamartanō`: Anger itself is not here condemned as sin, but the will must act quickly to prevent it from becoming sin — the verse locates the danger in allowing anger to persist unchecked. — keywords: `anger unchecked`, `will acting`, `emotion persisting`, `sin potential`, `urgency moral`
- **vc=37535** 1Jo 3:8 `G0264 hamartanō`: A habitual practice of sinning discloses the person's allegiance at the deepest level — it aligns the self with the devil, whose sinning is originary, making sin a mark of belonging rather than a mere act. — keywords: `allegiance deepest`, `sin habitual`, `belonging revealed`, `practice sinning`, `identity disclosed`, `defection constitutive`
- **vc=37536** 1Jo 3:9 `G0264 hamartanō`: Divine birth transforms the inner constitution: God's seed abiding in the person makes sustained sinning structurally incompatible with who that person now is at their core. — keywords: `birth transforming`, `constitution renewed`, `seed abiding`, `sinning incompatible`, `nature regenerate`, `inner transformation`
- **vc=37537** 1Jo 5:16 `G0264 hamartanō`: Sin is differentiated by its direction and consequence: some sin does not sever life, and intercession can restore the sinning brother; but sin that leads to death lies beyond the scope of that intercessory remedy. — keywords: `sin differentiated`, `intercession restoring`, `direction mortal`, `consequence terminal`, `sin severing`, `remedy limited`
- **vc=37538** 1Jo 5:18 `G0264 hamartanō`: The one born of God does not keep sinning because Christ himself protects that person, so that the evil one cannot gain a foothold — sin is prevented by an external guardian reinforcing the inner new birth. — keywords: `birth protecting`, `guardian external`, `sin prevented`, `evil repelled`, `new birth reinforced`, `protection divine`

### M10-V

#### M10-V-VCG-01 (32 verses)

- **vc=19134** Gen 41:9 `H2399 chet`: The cupbearer recalls his offenses to Pharaoh—the term refers to a remembered failure of duty that now resurfaces in his conscience at a moment of moral relevance. — keywords: `memory surfacing`, `conscience awakening`, `failure remembered`, `guilt resurfacing`, `duty neglected`
- **vc=19135** Lev 19:17 `H2399 chet`: Sin is located in the will and conscience: harboring hatred in the heart without honest rebuke risks incurring sin against one's neighbor, showing sin as something that can arise from inner attitudes left unaddressed. — keywords: `hatred inner`, `heart concealing`, `conscience neglected`, `rebuke withheld`, `sin incurred`, `will unaddressed`
- **vc=19136** Lev 20:20 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is the guilt borne personally by those who engage in sexual relations with an uncle's wife — a violation that brings the consequences of dying childless, linking sin directly to its punitive outcome. — keywords: `guilt personal`, `sin bearing`, `violation sexual`, `consequence punitive`, `liability carried`
- **vc=19159** Lev 22:9 `H2399 chet`: Sin is the moral and cultic liability priests incur by neglecting God's charge regarding holy things — negligence in sacred duty becomes a sin that can result in death, showing sin as arising from failure of responsible will. — keywords: `negligence cultic`, `will failing`, `guilt incurred`, `duty neglected`, `liability fatal`, `conscience derelict`
- **vc=19160** Lev 24:15 `H2399 chet`: Sin is the personal guilt borne by anyone who curses God — the act of blasphemy against God is named as a sin that the offender must carry, indicating it is a moral liability that rests directly on the individual. — keywords: `blasphemy`, `guilt personal`, `sin bearing`, `liability direct`, `defection verbal`
- **vc=19137** Num 9:13 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is something a person 'bears' as a consequence of willful neglect of a sacred obligation; the image of carrying one's sin indicates that unaddressed guilt remains on the person and leads to being cut off from the community. — keywords: `sin bearing`, `guilt unresolved`, `neglect willful`, `obligation ignored`, `exclusion communal`, `liability carried`
- **vc=19138** Num 18:22 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is the mortal danger incurred when an unauthorized person draws near the sacred tent; 'bearing sin and dying' shows that sin is not merely moral failure but a condition of incompatibility with holiness that produces lethal consequence. — keywords: `holiness incompatibility`, `guilt bearing`, `transgression lethal`, `boundary violation`, `sacred proximity`
- **vc=19161** Num 18:32 `H2399 chet`: Sin is avoidable if the Levites honor God's standards for the offerings; the warning 'bear no sin' by contributing the best shows that sin attaches to careless or disrespectful handling of what is holy, and right action prevents incurring it. — keywords: `sin avoidable`, `guilt preventable`, `reverence required`, `handling careless`, `holiness profaned`
- **vc=19162** Num 27:3 `H2399 chet`: The daughters distinguish their father's death as being 'for his own sin,' not Korah's rebellion; this individuates guilt, showing that sin is personally owned and that one person's moral failure is separate and distinct from collective transgression. — keywords: `guilt individuated`, `sin personal`, `accountability separate`, `collective distinguished`, `ownership moral`
- **vc=19139** Deu 15:9 `H2399 chet`: Sin originates in the heart — an 'unworthy thought' that leads to a grudging eye and refusal to give; this verse traces the sin of stinginess toward the poor from its inner source in the heart's calculation, showing conscience implicated before any outward act. — keywords: `heart calculating`, `thought unworthy`, `stinginess inner`, `eye grudging`, `sin originating`, `conscience implicated`
- **vc=19670** Deu 19:15 `H2399 chet`: Sin is the offense in connection with which a witness must testify; the verse does not elaborate on inner content but establishes that sin requires corroborated human testimony to be legally actionable, situating it within a framework of communal accountability. — keywords: `accountability communal`, `sin verified`, `testimony required`, `guilt established`, `witness corroborated`
- **vc=19140** Deu 21:22 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is a capital offense committed by an individual—an act so grave that it warrants death and public display as a deterrent, marking the person as one who crossed the ultimate moral boundary. — keywords: `transgression capital`, `boundary ultimate`, `sin grave`, `death deserved`, `display deterrent`
- **vc=19669** Deu 22:26 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is a capital moral offense that the coerced young woman has not committed; her innocence is affirmed by the involuntary nature of the act, contrasting with the aggressor's culpable will. — keywords: `innocence coerced`, `will absent`, `guilt negated`, `culpability voluntary`, `aggressor willful`
- **vc=19141** Deu 23:21 `H2399 chet`: Sin here arises from a failure of the will to follow through on a vow made to God; delay in fulfilling a freely made commitment constitutes a moral fault that God holds the person accountable for. — keywords: `will failing`, `vow delayed`, `commitment broken`, `accountability divine`, `sin incurred`
- **vc=19142** Deu 23:22 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is the guilt incurred by making a vow and not keeping it; by contrast, refraining from vowing altogether avoids the condition of sin, showing that sin attaches to broken intentional commitment. — keywords: `commitment unbroken`, `sin avoided`, `vow withheld`, `guilt preventable`, `will restrained`
- **vc=19143** Deu 24:15 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is incurred by failing to pay a poor worker's wages on time; when the worker cries to God in need, the employer's neglect becomes a moral fault that God registers against them. — keywords: `neglect sinful`, `cry divine`, `neighbor wronged`, `guilt registered`, `sin social`
- **vc=19144** Deu 24:16 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is strictly personal—each person dies for their own transgression, not another's; moral accountability is located within the individual, not transferred across family lines. — keywords: `guilt personal`, `accountability individual`, `sin nontransferable`, `responsibility own`, `death deserved`
- **vc=19155** 2Ki 10:29 `H2399 chet`: Jehu's failure to depart from Jeroboam's sins—specifically the golden calves at Bethel and Dan—shows that sin can remain as a fixed object of continued practice even in a reforming leader. — keywords: `sin fixed`, `turning absent`, `practice continued`, `defection persistent`, `reform incomplete`
- **vc=19156** 2Ki 14:6 `H2399 chet`: The law forbids executing children for fathers' sins, establishing that sin is personally owned—each individual dies for his own sin, not another's, locating moral responsibility in the individual. — keywords: `responsibility personal`, `guilt individual`, `accountability owned`, `sin personal`, `autonomy moral`
- **vc=19157** 2Ch 25:4 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is explicitly personal and non-transferable—each person dies for their own sin, not another's; the verse limits guilt to the individual moral agent, showing sin as a specifically owned inner-moral accountability. — keywords: `guilt personal`, `accountability individual`, `non-transferable sin`, `agency moral`, `liability owned`
- **vc=19132** Psa 51:5 `H2399 chet` ★: Sin is present at the very moment of conception, showing it as a condition inherited at the origin of personal existence, not merely an act chosen but a state the person is born into from the beginning. — keywords: `sin inherited`, `condition natal`, `origin corrupted`, `nature fallen`, `existence tainted`
- **vc=19145** Psa 51:9 `H2399 chet`: Sins are viewed by God's face that sees them; the psalmist asks God to hide his face from them, showing sin as a visible moral reality before God's gaze that requires divine non-recognition for the person to find peace. — keywords: `visibility divine`, `gaze averted`, `exposure feared`, `blotting sought`, `recognition withheld`
- **vc=19146** Psa 103:10 `H2399 chet`: Sin is something that could warrant proportional divine punishment, but God mercifully withholds what is deserved; the verse reveals sin as incurring a debt that grace exceeds. — keywords: `debt unpaid`, `punishment withheld`, `grace exceeding`, `mercy undeserved`, `guilt unrequited`
- **vc=19153** Ecc 10:4 `H2399 chet`: Great offenses or sins can be laid to rest by calmness — the inner quality of composure when facing a ruler's anger counteracts the escalation that sin produces, showing sin as something that can be de-escalated by wise inner self-control. — keywords: `composure restraining`, `self-control inner`, `calmness counteracting`, `escalation prevented`, `offense de-escalated`
- **vc=19158** Isa 31:7 `H2399 chet`: Sin is located in the hands as the active agents of idolatry — the people crafted silver and gold idols, making sin a product of deliberate human making rather than passive failure. — keywords: `idolatry crafted`, `sin deliberate`, `will active`, `hands sinful`, `agency human`
- **vc=19147** Isa 38:17 `H2399 chet`: Sin is cast behind God's back — it is treated as something fully removed from divine memory and reckoning, contrasting with the bitterness it had caused, now replaced by delivered life. — keywords: `sin forgotten`, `guilt removed`, `divine forgetting`, `bitterness past`, `restoration relational`
- **vc=19148** Isa 53:12 `H2399 chet`: The servant bore the sin of many as a weight requiring intercession — he identified with transgressors to the point of death, taking on the sin that separated them from God. — keywords: `sin borne`, `substitution vicarious`, `intercession active`, `guilt transferred`, `identification transgressor`
- **vc=19154** Lam 1:8 `H2399 chet`: Sin's gravity ('grievously') is measured by its effects: filth, loss of honor, exposed nakedness, and inner groaning; the verse shows sin as a deeply shameful inner condition whose consequences manifest outwardly in humiliation. — keywords: `shame deep`, `groaning inner`, `nakedness exposed`, `disgrace felt`, `sin grievous`, `humiliation bearing`
- **vc=19149** Lam 3:39 `H2399 chet`: Sins bring deserved punishment, so complaining about it is presented as unreasonable for a still-living person; the verse grounds sin's consequence in a moral order where suffering for one's own sin is just, not cause for grievance. — keywords: `punishment deserved`, `complaint suppressed`, `sin consequential`, `moral order accepted`, `suffering just`, `grievance futile`
- **vc=19150** Eze 23:49 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is borne as a penalty: Israel must carry the full weight of her sinful idolatry returned upon herself, so that through suffering it she comes to know God. — keywords: `penalty bearing`, `sin returned`, `suffering knowing`, `idolatry consequence`, `burden borne`, `knowledge divine`
- **vc=19151** Dan 9:16 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is identified as the cause of divine anger resting on Jerusalem; the people's sins and their fathers' iniquities together have made the city a byword, showing sin's corporate, generational, destructive reach. — keywords: `sin corporate`, `guilt generational`, `anger divine`, `shame communal`, `byword becoming`, `inheritance moral`
- **vc=19152** Hos 12:8 `H2399 chet`: Sin here is something Ephraim self-deceptively denies — his wealth convinces him no sin or iniquity can be found in him — revealing sin as a moral reality that prosperity blinds the conscience to, though it is still present. — keywords: `self-deception`, `conscience blinded`, `denial willful`, `prosperity distorting`, `sin unacknowledged`, `awareness suppressed`

#### M10-V-VCG-02 (9 verses)

- **vc=19183** Gen 20:9 `H2401 cha.ta.ah`: Abraham's deception placed a great sin upon Abimelech's household—sin here is a moral burden transferred by another's wrongful act, causing communal harm. — keywords: `sin transferred`, `burden communal`, `guilt imposed`, `innocence violated`, `harm relational`
- **vc=19184** Exo 32:21 `H2401 cha.ta.ah`: Moses confronts Aaron for bringing a great sin upon the people; the sin is a collective moral weight loaded onto the community by Aaron's leadership failure in permitting idolatry. — keywords: `sin transferred`, `leadership failure`, `guilt collective`, `burden imposed`, `accountability confronted`

### M10-W

#### M10-W-VCG-01 (12 verses)

- **vc=29692** Exo 29:36 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: The daily sin offering is offered explicitly for atonement; atonement here is the purpose of the sacrifice, covering the defilement that prevents the altar from functioning as a holy meeting point. — keywords: `atonement covering`, `defilement ritual`, `purification daily`, `holiness restored`, `mediation priestly`
- **vc=29693** Exo 30:10 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: Annual atonement made with sin-offering blood on the altar's horns consecrates it as most holy; the once-a-year rite covers accumulated impurity so the altar remains a valid place of divine encounter. — keywords: `atonement annual`, `impurity accumulated`, `blood covering`, `holiness maintained`, `mediation priestly`
- **vc=29694** Exo 30:16 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: The atonement money given for the tent of meeting brings Israel to remembrance before God and makes atonement for their lives; ransom payment functions as the means of covering the moral debt that separates the people from God. — keywords: `ransom payment`, `debt moral`, `remembrance divine`, `atonement communal`, `life covered`
- **vc=19350** Lev 10:17 `H2403H chat.tat`: The sin offering is described as most holy and given to the priests specifically so they can bear the congregation's iniquity — the uneaten offering represents a failure of the priestly mediatory duty to address the people's sin. — keywords: `iniquity bearing`, `mediation priestly`, `duty neglected`, `intercession failed`, `burden corporate`
- **vc=19351** Lev 10:19 `H2403H chat.tat`: The sin offering ritual is presented as a mediatory act requiring proper inner disposition; Aaron implies that performing it while personally stricken might render it unacceptable, linking ritual efficacy to interior condition. — keywords: `disposition interior`, `ritual efficacy`, `grief disrupting`, `conscience hesitating`, `worthiness questioned`, `approval sought`
- **vc=29691** Lev 23:27 `H3725 kip.pu.rim` ★: The Day of Atonement is a sacred annual occasion requiring self-affliction and a food offering — it is the communal event through which Israel's accumulated sin is addressed and moral standing before God is restored. — keywords: `self affliction`, `guilt communal`, `standing restored`, `conscience corporate`, `atonement annual`
- **vc=29695** Lev 23:28 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: The Day of Atonement demands complete rest from all work, underscoring that the act of making atonement before God is incompatible with ordinary human activity — the whole day is set apart for the work of reconciliation. — keywords: `work ceasing`, `reconciliation active`, `atonement exclusive`, `rest obligatory`, `focus divine`
- **vc=29696** Lev 25:9 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: The Day of Atonement is the fixed annual day marked by a trumpet blast throughout the land, signaling that reconciliation with God is not a private act but a national proclamation with communal and temporal significance. — keywords: `proclamation communal`, `reconciliation national`, `atonement annual`, `awareness collective`, `signaling public`
- **vc=29697** Num 5:8 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: Atonement here is a required ritual offering (the ram) that restores a broken relationship with God when no human recipient exists for restitution, showing it functions as the necessary inner-relational repair between the guilty party and the Lord. — keywords: `relational repair`, `atonement required`, `guilt unresolved`, `restitution redirected`, `reconciliation divine`
- **vc=29698** Num 29:11 `H3725 kip.pu.rim`: The sin offering of atonement is a distinct, scheduled ritual provision; it points to the ongoing moral liability of the community before God, showing that atonement must be regularly maintained and not just addressed in moments of acute wrongdoing. — keywords: `liability ongoing`, `atonement scheduled`, `sin communal`, `provision ritual`, `maintenance moral`
- **vc=19352** 2Ch 29:23 `H2403H chat.tat`: The sin offering here is a ritual object—goats brought before the assembly—over which hands are laid; sin is conceived as a transferable moral burden that can be ceremonially placed onto a substitute presented before king and community. — keywords: `burden transferable`, `substitution ritual`, `hands laying`, `guilt displaced`, `assembly communal`
- **vc=19353** 2Ch 29:24 `H2403H chat.tat`: The sin offering here is a priestly act using sacrificial blood on the altar to make atonement for all Israel; sin is the moral liability that requires a blood-mediated ritual remedy ordered by the king on behalf of the whole nation. — keywords: `atonement blood`, `liability corporate`, `substitution priestly`, `remedy ritual`, `nation cleansed`

#### M10-W-VCG-02 (12 verses)

- **vc=19185** Exo 32:30 `H2401 cha.ta.ah`: The great sin is something Moses hopes to atone for before God; sin here is an offense requiring specific remedial action to repair the ruptured covenant between Israel and the Lord. — keywords: `sin acknowledged`, `intercession priestly`, `atonement sought`, `covenant rupture`, `hope repair`
- **vc=19186** Exo 32:31 `H2401 cha.ta.ah`: Moses names the making of golden gods a great sin as he intercedes before the Lord; sin here is the specific act of idolatry, named plainly as the moral content of what the people have done. — keywords: `idolatry named`, `sin confessed`, `intercession bold`, `guilt specific`, `conscience naming`
- **vc=19711** Mat 26:28 `G0266 hamartia`: Sin here is presented as a corporate burden requiring atoning blood; Jesus' shed blood establishes a covenant whose purpose is the forgiveness of the accumulated guilt of many. — keywords: `guilt corporate`, `atonement covenantal`, `burden accumulated`, `forgiveness blood`, `debt removed`
- **vc=37556** Mar 3:28 `G0265 hamartēma`: All sins and blasphemies spoken by people fall within the scope of divine forgiveness, indicating no ordinary moral or verbal failing places a person permanently beyond God's mercy. — keywords: `forgiveness scope`, `mercy universal`, `sin forgivable`, `guilt coverable`, `blasphemy covered`
- **vc=37555** Mar 3:29 `G0265 hamartēma`: Blasphemy against the Holy Spirit constitutes an eternal sin — a state of guilt with no exit — suggesting an inner condition of such deep opposition to the Spirit that forgiveness is never obtained. — keywords: `opposition permanent`, `guilt eternal`, `spirit resisted`, `hardening terminal`, `forgiveness impossible`, `defection irreversible`
- **vc=19701** Luk 7:47 `G0266 hamartia` ★: The woman's many sins are forgiven because she loved much — Jesus links the depth of inner gratitude and love to the magnitude of forgiveness received, making her sins the backdrop that measures the grace given. — keywords: `guilt magnitude`, `love responding`, `gratitude deep`, `forgiveness received`, `sin backdrop`
- **vc=19702** Luk 7:48 `G0266 hamartia`: Jesus directly declares the woman's sins forgiven, addressing her inner moral burden personally and authoritatively, releasing her from the guilt that had defined her social and spiritual identity. — keywords: `guilt released`, `burden lifted`, `identity transformed`, `forgiveness personal`, `sin declared`
- **vc=19679** Act 2:38 `G0266 hamartia`: Sins here are the accumulated offenses requiring forgiveness, which repentance and baptism in Jesus's name address—sin is the inner condition that must be resolved before the Spirit is received. — keywords: `repentance turning`, `sin accumulated`, `forgiveness received`, `condition resolved`, `cleansing prerequisite`
- **vc=40869** 2Cor 5:19 `G3900 paraptōma`: Trespasses are the offences that create alienation between humanity and God; God's reconciling act in Christ consists precisely in not counting these trespasses against people, absorbing them rather than imputing them. — keywords: `trespass absorbed`, `imputation withheld`, `alienation removed`, `guilt uncounted`, `reconciliation offered`
- **vc=40879** Eph 1:7 `G3900 paraptōma`: Trespasses are the moral offenses from which believers need redemption; they are forgiven through Christ's blood, showing their guilt-incurring weight that required atoning sacrifice. — keywords: `trespass forgiven`, `guilt redeemed`, `blood atoning`, `grace receiving`, `weight removed`
- **vc=19685** Col 1:14 `G0266 hamartia`: Sins are the offenses requiring forgiveness, which redemption through Christ provides — the verse frames sin as the debt or moral deficit that makes redemption necessary. — keywords: `sin debt`, `forgiveness received`, `moral deficit`, `redemption need`, `guilt released`
- **vc=40881** Col 2:13 `G3900 paraptōma`: Trespasses are the cause of spiritual death — the uncircumcised inner person is dead in them, and divine forgiveness of all trespasses is what makes alive, showing their total grip on the inner life. — keywords: `spiritual deadness`, `trespass grip`, `inner death`, `divine quickening`, `forgiveness total`, `conscience released`

#### M10-W-VCG-03 (10 verses)

- **vc=19197** Exo 32:30 `H2403B chat.tat` ★: Moses declares the people have sinned greatly and announces an attempt at atonement; the sin is framed as a severe moral wrong against God requiring priestly intercession to potentially repair. — keywords: `sin gravity`, `intercession priestly`, `covenant rupture`, `atonement attempted`, `mediation urgent`
- **vc=19201** Lev 4:3 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sin here is a specific committed act by the priest that requires a defined ritual remedy — a bull without blemish — establishing that sin creates an objective moral debt demanding satisfaction before God. — keywords: `sin objective`, `guilt transferred`, `debt ritual`, `remedy prescribed`, `transgression committed`
- **vc=19202** Lev 4:14 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sin is presented as a fact that 'becomes known' to the assembly; once recognized, it demands a communal sin-offering response, showing sin as an objective moral reality requiring corporate acknowledgment and remedy. — keywords: `sin surfacing`, `recognition corporate`, `conscience communal`, `remedy obligated`, `sin objective`
- **vc=19207** Lev 5:6 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sin is the moral wrong for which a compensation offering is brought; it is something 'committed' by the individual, and the sin offering is the prescribed means by which priestly mediation achieves atonement. — keywords: `sin committed`, `compensation offered`, `atonement priestly`, `guilt discharged`, `debt moral`
- **vc=19208** Lev 5:10 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sin here is the specific act for which atonement is made and forgiveness granted; its pairing with 'committed' confirms sin's personal, volitional character even when unintentional, requiring priestly intercession for resolution. — keywords: `transgression volitional`, `guilt resolved`, `atonement priestly`, `forgiveness granted`, `liability personal`
- **vc=19210** Lev 10:19 `H2403B chat.tat`: Aaron questions whether eating the sin offering under circumstances of personal grief and tragedy would have been acceptable to God, showing sin as something whose ritual remedy is inextricably tied to the inner state of the officiant. — keywords: `grief inner`, `ritual worthiness`, `conscience questioning`, `disposition interior`, `approval divine`, `doubt officiating`
- **vc=19211** Lev 16:16 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sin is grouped with transgressions and uncleannesses as the collective moral pollution of Israel that defiles even the sanctuary, requiring atonement to cleanse the holy space where God dwells among the people. — keywords: `pollution collective`, `transgression accumulated`, `defilement sanctuary`, `uncleanness moral`, `atonement corporate`
- **vc=19213** Lev 16:30 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sins are what make Israel unclean before God, and the Day of Atonement provides the comprehensive cleansing of all of them, restoring the people to a state of purity and right standing before the Lord. — keywords: `cleansing comprehensive`, `purity restored`, `standing restored`, `uncleanness removed`, `guilt cleared`
- **vc=19215** Lev 19:22 `H2403B chat.tat`: Sin is named as the specific act committed that the atonement offering addresses; once atonement is made, forgiveness is granted, showing sin as a defined moral liability that priestly mediation can resolve. — keywords: `liability defined`, `guilt personal`, `atonement resolving`, `forgiveness granted`, `offense specific`
- **vc=19677** Act 10:43 `G0266 hamartia`: Belief in Jesus brings forgiveness of sins through his name—sin is a universal human condition the prophets anticipated would be resolved, available to everyone who believes. — keywords: `belief receiving`, `forgiveness universal`, `sin condition`, `faith accessing`, `debt resolved`

### M10-X

#### M10-X-VCG-01 (8 verses)

- **vc=18970** 1Ki 8:47 `H2398 cha.ta`: The exiles' confession 'we have sinned and acted perversely and wickedly' in captivity is an inward turning of the heart, showing that genuine acknowledgment of sin—spoken from conscience—is the first step toward restoration. — keywords: `heart turning`, `confession communal`, `guilt acknowledged`, `repentance inward`, `restoration seeking`
- **vc=19061** Psa 78:17 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning is shown as a persistent, willful act of the will directed against God even amid his provision; it is compounded by open rebellion against the Most High in the wilderness. — keywords: `sin escalating`, `rebellion willful`, `defection persistent`, `provision ignored`, `will hardening`
- **vc=19062** Psa 78:32 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning persisted despite witnessed wonders, revealing it as rooted in unbelief of the heart; the people's refusal to believe God's works kept them in ongoing sin against him. — keywords: `unbelief rooted`, `sin persistent`, `heart refusing`, `wonder rejected`, `defection habitual`, `faith absent`
- **vc=19065** Isa 43:27 `H2398 cha.ta` ★: Sinning is traced back to the first father — establishing sin as an ancestral, generational failure in the will that has persisted through appointed mediators who also transgressed. — keywords: `ancestral sin`, `generational failing`, `transgression inherited`, `origin traced`, `mediators defecting`
- **vc=19066** Isa 64:5 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning happened in response to God's anger, and the people have persisted in it a long time — sin here is both a response to divine displeasure and a prolonged condition of the will that raises doubt about salvation. — keywords: `persistence sinning`, `duration prolonged`, `will habituated`, `salvation doubted`, `anger response`
- **vc=19075** Isa 65:20 `H2398 cha.ta`: To sin is here the defining identity of the person who dies cursed at a hundred years old; sinning is contrasted with long, blessed life, marking the sinner as one whose inner rebellion forfeits the flourishing promised in the new creation. — keywords: `identity cursed`, `flourishing forfeited`, `rebellion inner`, `blessing lost`, `curse defined`
- **vc=18962** Jer 8:14 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning against God is acknowledged as the reason God has given them poisoned water and doom; the people's inner transgression is recognized as the cause of their desperate, hopeless situation. — keywords: `doom recognized`, `sin acknowledged`, `despair inner`, `judgment accepted`, `hopelessness`
- **vc=19047** Eze 37:23 `H2398 cha.ta`: Sinning here describes Israel's past backsliding into idolatry; God promises to save them from it and cleanse them, showing sin as a defilement that requires divine rescue and purification. — keywords: `backsliding past`, `defilement cleansed`, `rescue divine`, `idolatry renounced`, `purification promised`, `restoration covenantal`

## §9. Set-aside reasons (Phase 1 + Phase 8.5)

**Total set-aside verses with reason:** 25

- **vc=65830** Rev 8:9 `G1311 diaftheirō` — diaftheirō used of physical destruction of ships, not moral corruption — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65831** Rev 11:18 `G1311 diaftheirō` — diaftheirō used of physical/eschatological destruction of earth-destroyers, not moral corruption of persons — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65832** Num 23:21 `H0205H a.ven` — a.ven used of external calamity/misfortune in a blessing oracle, not the inner moral-trouble state of a transgressor — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=12427** Deu 26:14 `H0205H a.ven` — Phase 3 BOUNDARY verdict. The 4 a.ven (H0205H) active verses (Deu 26:14, Job 5:6, Psa 90:10, Pro 22:8) plus the Phase 1 parked borderline Pro 12:21 are semantically mixed between moral-trouble-as-iniquity-consequence and general circumstantial suffering / grief / mortal burden. No coherent M10 (sin-as-act/state) register survives. Set aside from M10. The term mti_id stays in M10 with no relevant verses. If M03 (grief) or M20 (distress) later opens these verses, they may be picked up via cross-cluster co-reference.
- **vc=12428** Job 5:6 `H0205H a.ven` — Phase 3 BOUNDARY verdict. No coherent M10 (sin-as-act/state) register survives. Set aside from M10. The term mti_id stays in M10 with no relevant verses. - **vc=65834** Jer 4:15 `H0205H a.ven` — a.ven used of announced military calamity/disaster, not a sinner's inner moral-trouble state — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65835** Hos 9:4 `H0205H a.ven` — a.ven used in a ritual-defilement/mourning context, not the inner moral-collapse state of a transgressor — belongs to M10c defilement.

- **vc=65839** Joe 1:18 `H0816 a.sham` — a.sham used of animals suffering/perishing from drought, not of moral guilt or transgression — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65841** Ecc 5:6 `H2254B cha.val` — cha.val used of physical destruction of one's works by divine anger, not guilt-agony of the inner being — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65842** Song 2:15 `H2254B cha.val` — cha.val used of physical spoiling of vineyards by foxes, not guilt-agony — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.

- **vc=65845** Isa 54:16 `H2254B cha.val` — cha.val used of a divinely-created ravager causing physical destruction, not guilt-agony — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65846** Mic 2:10 `H2256D che.vel` — Phase 3 BOUNDARY verdict. The single che.vel (H2256D) verse Mic 2:10 names uncleanness-as-cause-of-destruction. Primary register is M10c (Defilement/Impurity), the sibling cluster carved out at the 2026-05-22 3-way split. M10c picks this verse up via cross-cluster co-reference (CROSS_CLUSTER_HANDOFF observation recorded).
- **vc=65847** Num 8:7 `H2403I chat.tat` — chat.tat used in the sense of purification-water for ritual cleansing of Levites, not the punishment/consequence-of-sin sense owned by H2403I — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=37244** Pro 31:8 `H2475 cha.loph` — wrong_face

- **vc=65849** Job 21:34 `H4604 ma.al` — ma.al used in the sense of 'falsehood/deception' in a wisdom dispute, not covenant-unfaithfulness or sacrilegious transgression — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65850** Job 12:19 `H5557 sa.laph` — sa.laph used of God overthrowing the powerful (physical/political reversal), not perverting justice or morality — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
- **vc=65851** Isa 24:1 `H5753A a.vah` — a.vah used of physical twisting/distortion of the earth's surface, not moral perversion or iniquity — outside M10 sin/guilt/transgression scope.
